<h3><a name="page-1063694">CB10_0001</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Sept. 13, 1888.</p>
<p>BALDWIN &amp; EMERSON<span class='line-break'> </span>BOSTON.</p>
<p>Dear Sirs:-</p>
<p>At what price will you deliver at this cemetery two <span class='line-break'> </span>North River flags 8'-8" x 6'-10" x 0'-3". They are for cover<span class='line-break'></span>ing burial vaults, so the edges should be broken to line and one <span class='line-break'> </span>surface flat.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours ,<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
<p>4435-5</p>
<p>Sept.13,1888.</p>
<p>[DL?] CHARLES E. INCHES,<span class='line-break'> </span>BOSTON.</p>
<p>[Dear] Sir:-</p>
<p>Your note is received and will have immediate attention.<span class='line-break'> </span>[If?] [the?] corporation does the setting the whole can be done at once.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours ,<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1063695">
<h3><a name="page-1063695">CB10_0002</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>2</p>
<p>Sept. 14, 1888</p>
<p>HIGHLAND SLATE M. CO.,<span class='line-break'> </span>BOSTON</p>
<p>Dear Sirs: -</p>
<p>Your note of 12th is received, and I have seen your <span class='line-break'> </span>agent in regard to the additional slate covers you wish me to order<span class='line-break'> </span>He handed me the following list:</p>
<p><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>7 covers</th> <th>3' -  9" x 2' -  8"<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>3 [covers]</td> <td>3 -  9  x  2  -  6</td> </tr> <tr><td>3 [covers]</td> <td>3 -  7  x  2  -  8</td> </tr> <tr><td>6 [covers]</td> <td>3 -  7  x  2  -  5</td> </tr> <tr><td>3 [covers]</td> <td>3 -  7  x  2  -  6</td> </tr> <tr><td>10 [covers]</td> <td>3 -  9  x  2  -10</td> </tr> <tr><td>7 [covers]</td> <td>3 -  5  x  2  -  6</td> </tr> <tr><td><u>8 [covers]</u></td> <td><u>3  -  3  x  2  -  6  ( not wanted)</u></td> </tr> <tr><td>17 [covers]</td> <td>3 - 9   x  2 - 10</td> </tr> <tr><td>9 [covers]</td> <td>3 -  6  x  2 -   6</td> </tr> <tr><td>5 [covers]</td> <td>3  - 7  x  2  -  8</td> </tr> <tr><td>4 [covers]</td> <td>3  - 7  x  2  -  4</td> </tr> <tr><td>12 [covers]</td> <td>3 - 9   x  2  -  6</td> </tr> <tr><td><u>21 [covers]</u></td> <td><u>3 - 3   x  2 -  6 (not wanted)</u></td> </tr> </tbody> </table> The lots of 8 and 21 pieces 3'-3" x 2'-6" are not wanted<span class='line-break'> </span>as this is a size we have no use for.  The other pieces I will take <span class='line-break'> </span>if of the same quality as the slate already delivered, and at the <span class='line-break'> </span>same price delivered here.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1063696">
<h3><a name="page-1063696">CB10_0003</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Page 3</p>
<p>#17543-S</p>
<p>Sept. 14, 1888.</p>
<p>HENRY W. HOLBROOK, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>10 MILK ST., BOSTON.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>The gardener reports that the grave of which you com<span class='line-break'></span>plain was in poor condition when the other repairs were made, or in<span class='line-break'> </span>such condition that he did not think it well to take any myrtle<span class='line-break'> </span>from it as was done with the others.  To properly replant it will<span class='line-break'> </span>cost $7.00.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1063697">
<h3><a name="page-1063697">CB10_0004</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Page 4</p>
<p>#3082-S</p>
<p>Sept. 15, 1888.</p>
<p>MRS: C. B. WILSON,<span class='line-break'> </span>BOSTON.</p>
<p>Dear Madam:-</p>
<p>In regard to the charge for cleaning the stone on your<span class='line-break'> </span>lot, I find that the estimate given you in my letter of Sept. 10,<span class='line-break'> </span>1887 was $3.00, so that the bill sent you is under not over the<span class='line-break'> </span>estimate.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
<p>#1169-S</p>
<p>Sept. 15, 1888.</p>
<p>FRANCIS &amp; COMPANY<span class='line-break'> </span>SYRACUSE, N.Y.</p>
<p>Dear Sirs:-</p>
<p>The Fawlkner monument is I believe made of Tennessee<span class='line-break'> </span>marble. The makers Evans &amp; Tombs, Huntington Ave. Bridge, Boston<span class='line-break'> </span>will I have no doubt give particulars if you write them.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1063698">
<h3><a name="page-1063698">CB10_0005</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Page 5</p>
<p>#2620-S</p>
<p>Sept. 15, 1888.</p>
<p>DAVID H. GILE, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>#1837 INDIANA AVE., CHICAGO</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>Your letter of 10th has been forwarded me by our Treas<span class='line-break'></span>urer.  Lot #2620 on Orchis pah is triangular in shape, and con<span class='line-break'></span>tains 150 sq. feet.  The two interments now there were made before<span class='line-break'> </span>we kept the exact locations of the bodies, so that without digging<span class='line-break'> </span>down it is impossible to tell how much space is left.  From the<span class='line-break'> </span>appearance of the surface there may be room for two more graves,<span class='line-break'> </span>but the surface indications are not always reliable.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
<p>#3125-S</p>
<p>Sept. 17, 1888.</p>
<p>MRS. M. A. BREWER,<span class='line-break'> </span>#219 Cottage St., Dorchester.</p>
<p>Dear Madam:-</p>
<p>Your note is received.  Two catacombs for future use<span class='line-break'> </span>if built side by side would cost $40.00, if one is built over the<span class='line-break'> </span>other, the lower one would have 8 inch walls and the cost would be<span class='line-break'> </span>$45.00.  I suppose the Turpin lot #3125 is the one you refer to.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1063699">
<h3><a name="page-1063699">CB10_0006</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Page 6</p>
<p>Sept. 17, 1888.</p>
<p>BALDWIN &amp; EMERSON,<span class='line-break'> </span>BOSTON.</p>
<p>Dear Sirs:-</p>
<p>In asking the price of the North River stone I gave the<span class='line-break'> </span>wrong width.  The whole width of two stones is 6' - 10", so that the<span class='line-break'> </span>two stones wanted will be each 8' - 8" x 3' - 5" x 0' - 3".  Please<span class='line-break'> </span>give me your price for these also say if there would be any diff<span class='line-break'></span>erence if they were only 2 inches thick instead of 3 inches.<span class='line-break'> </span>Your early reply will oblige.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1063700">
<h3><a name="page-1063700">CB10_0007</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Page 7</p>
<p>S</p>
<p>Sept. 19, 1888.</p>
<p>THE NEW ENGLAND MONUMENT CO.<span class='line-break'> </span>NEW YORK.</p>
<p>Dear Sirs:-</p>
<p>Your note of 17th is received, and I have forwarded an<span class='line-break'> </span>application for a permit as directed.  If when you make a contract<span class='line-break'> </span>for work in this cemetary you will ask the parties to put themselve<span class='line-break'></span>es in communication with our Boston Office (#5 Pemberton Sq.) the<span class='line-break'> </span>Secy will issue a permit on the application of the proprietor of<span class='line-break'> </span>the lot.  This permit should be forwarded here or brought by the<span class='line-break'> </span>teamster with his first load.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>#2765-S</p>
<p>Sept. 19, 1888.</p>
<p>MRS. R. A. VINAL,<span class='line-break'> </span>SOMERVILLE.</p>
<p>Dear Madam:-</p>
<p>Your note is received.  None of the marbles stand well<span class='line-break'> </span>out of doors, and the more elaborate the work the greater the lia<span class='line-break'></span>bility to decay.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1063701">
<h3><a name="page-1063701">CB10_0008</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Page 8</p>
<p>#91-S</p>
<p>Sept 19, 1888</p>
<p>J. H. ELLISON, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>WALTHAM.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>I have just seen your lot, and think it will compare<span class='line-break'> </span>favorably with lots that have the same provision for care.  It may<span class='line-break'> </span>be that you made the comparison with some of our perpetual care<span class='line-break'> </span>lots, but there the amounts are large enough to cover special care,<span class='line-break'> </span>repairs and watering, and these will of course look better.  I will<span class='line-break'> </span>have some grass seed sown in your lot which will help it somewhat.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
<p>#4144-S</p>
<p>Sept. 19, 1888.</p>
<p>MRS. M. L. PIERPONT CROSBY,<span class='line-break'> </span>#3 Chauncey St., Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Madam:-</p>
<p>I am requested by the New England Monument Co. to for<span class='line-break'></span>ward the enclosed application for permit to you for signature.  If<span class='line-break'> </span>enclosed in the envelope herewith sent and forwarded to our Boston<span class='line-break'> </span>office if will have attention.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1063702">
<h3><a name="page-1063702">CB10_0009</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>page 9</p>
<p>2746-S</p>
<p>Sept. 19, 1888.</p>
<p>S.A. DENIO, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>Your note of 12th is received.  I have made enquiry as <span class='line-break'> </span>to the North River stone but am unable to get a quotation as low as <span class='line-break'> </span>you give.  It is not often that we need this stone, so that we<span class='line-break'> </span>would not be likely to get it at a low figure; would it not be well <span class='line-break'> </span>therefore for you to procure the stone and send it here when we can <span class='line-break'> </span>set it.  The size needed is an odd one, and I have not found a <span class='line-break'> </span>dealer in Boston who has it.  If the projection is 2 inches each <span class='line-break'> </span>stone will require to be 8' - 8" x 3' - 5" x 0' -  3". In making an <span class='line-break'> </span>interment it will be very awkward to handle so large a stone.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1063703">
<h3><a name="page-1063703">CB10_0010</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>10</p>
<p>#4629-S</p>
<p>Sept. 19, 1888.</p>
<p>JOHN H. McCARR, Esq:<span class='line-break'></span>Vine St., Somerville.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>There is a chair on your lot that is quite rusty, and <span class='line-break'> </span>I would suggest that it be painted or removed.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours, <span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
<p>#4010-S</p>
<p>Sept. 19, 1888.</p>
<p>MRS. C. B. CUMMMINGS,<span class='line-break'> </span>#6 Allston St., Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Madam:-</p>
<p>There are a chair and vase on your lot that are quite <span class='line-break'> </span>rusty,  I would suggest that they be either painted or removed.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1063704">
<h3><a name="page-1063704">CB10_0011</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>11</p>
<p>S</p>
<p>Sept. 19, 1888.</p>
<p>HIGHLAND SLATE MNF. CO.,<span class='line-break'> </span>BOSTON.</p>
<p>Dear Sirs:-</p>
<p>Thirteen peices of the last lot of slate sent here are <span class='line-break'> </span>too badly cracked and broken to be used here in any way, and should<span class='line-break'> </span>not have been sent.  Please remove them and send me corrected bill.</p>
<p>Sizes are as follows:</p>
<p>2 peices  3' - 7" x  2' - 6"</p>
<p>3      "        3' - 5" x  2'-6"</p>
<p>2      "        3' - 9" x 2' - 8"</p>
<p>2      "        3' - 6" x 2' - 6"</p>
<p>1      "        3' - 7"  x  2' - 4"</p>
<p>1      "        3" - 9" x  2' - 10"</p>
<p>1      "         3' - 7" x  2' - 8"</p>
<p>1      "        3' - 5" x  2' - 4"</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>

<div id="page-1063705">
<h3><a name="page-1063705">CB10_0012</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>12</p>
<p>Sept. 20, 1888</p>
<p>C. U. Cotting, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>Your note of yesterday is received.  The deposit named <span class='line-break'> </span>for the perpetual care with guaranty of the monument erected on the <span class='line-break'> </span>R.H.Eddy lot #4761 was two hundred and seventy five (275) dollars.</p>
<p>In front of the Eddy tomb on lot #362 (for the perpetual <span class='line-break'> </span>care of which you paid last January) are two shrubs much overgrown,<span class='line-break'> </span>and it would be better to remove them altogether, or replace with <span class='line-break'> </span>younger plants.  Is there any objections to so doing?</p>
<p>Yours truly,<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering    Supt.</p>
<p>#3585-S<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1063706">
<h3><a name="page-1063706">CB10_0013</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>13</p>
<p>#[523?]S</p>
<p>Sept. 20, 1888.</p>
<p>W. S. Carter,  Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Eliot St., Jamaica Plain.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>the fence on the Smith lot #328 is broken, and needs to<span class='line-break'> </span>be painted.  To repair it would cost $2.00, and to paint it $6.00.<span class='line-break'> </span>the lot would be improved by removing the fence altogether.</p>
<p>Fespectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
<p>#4220-S</p>
<p>Sept. 21, 1888.</p>
<p>O.H. Hayes, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>New York.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>the raised polished panel on the front of the die of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Henry Winkley monument is 4' - 5" high and 3' - 11" wide.  The name <span class='line-break'> </span>is cut in 4 inch square sunk letters, and the base of the letters <span class='line-break'> </span>is 9 1/2 inches from the top of the panel.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1063707">
<h3><a name="page-1063707">CB10_0014</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>14</p>
<p>Sept 24    8  [1888]</p>
<p>Philip T. Greely</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Enclosed find order <span class='line-break'> </span>for removing fence from lot 2349 on <span class='line-break'> </span>Sylvan Path.  If you wish the <span class='line-break'> </span>work done, please sign order and <span class='line-break'> </span>return to</p>
<p>Yours Resp'y<span class='line-break'> </span>J. W. Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span>per F.A. B.</p>
<p>Sept. 24    8   [1888]</p>
<p>Mrs. C. H. Parker</p>
<p>Dear Madam,</p>
<p>This is the proper<span class='line-break'> </span>season for planting the Crocuses<span class='line-break'> </span>mentioned on your annual order.<span class='line-break'> </span>Please inform me where you wish<span class='line-break'> </span>them planted and the order will<span class='line-break'> </span>be immediately attended to</p>
<p>Yours Resp'y.<span class='line-break'> </span>J. W. Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span>per F. A. B.</p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1063708">CB10_0015</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>15</p>
<p>Sept. 24   8   [1888]</p>
<p>Messrs A. McDonald &amp; Son<span class='line-break'> </span>Dear Sir<span class='line-break'> </span>The [floral borders?] on each side of <span class='line-break'> </span>the step on lot 3230 belong <span class='line-break'> </span>to the Corporation and I cannot <span class='line-break'> </span>therefore givy any permission to [?] them.</p>
<p>Yr truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J. W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
<p>Sept 26     8   [1888]<span class='line-break'> </span>Messers Evans and Tombs</p>
<p>Dear Sirs:<span class='line-break'> </span>Your order for a <span class='line-break'> </span>foundation in lot 1965 received,<span class='line-break'> </span>but as there are several graves in <span class='line-break'> </span>the rear of the lot which extend to within<span class='line-break'> </span>about one foot of centre of same,<span class='line-break'> </span>I think it will be necessary to <span class='line-break'> </span>place the monument farther front.</p>
<p>Yours Resp'y<span class='line-break'> </span>J. W. Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span>per F. A. B.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<div id="page-1063710">
<h3><a name="page-1063710">CB10_0017</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>17</p>
<p>Sept. 27      8   [1888]</p>
<p>Louis Jones and Son<span class='line-break'> </span>Dear Sirs:</p>
<p>The stone for the <span class='line-break'> </span>Eastburn lot has been delivered and<span class='line-break'> </span>I find on looking at it that several <span class='line-break'> </span>small pieces have been chipped<span class='line-break'> </span>from the base.  My men did not <span class='line-break'> </span>unload it.  The money to be <span class='line-break'> </span>paid to the persons delivering it has <span class='line-break'> </span>not yet been called for and I <span class='line-break'> </span>thought under the circumstances <span class='line-break'> </span>you might not wish it to be paid.</p>
<p>Yours Resp'y<span class='line-break'> </span>J. W. Lovering <span class='line-break'> </span>per F. A. B.</p>
<p>Sept. 28  8   [1888]</p>
<p>Dear Sirs:</p>
<p>Please send me your <span class='line-break'> </span>estimate for the undernoted quantities<span class='line-break'> </span>of grain etc.</p>
<p>58 Bush. No 1 White oats<span class='line-break'> </span>24     "        "    "  Yellow corn<span class='line-break'> </span>4       "        "    "  Cracked corm<span class='line-break'> </span>16     "        "    "   Meal</p>
<p>One half of each kind to be delivered <span class='line-break'> </span>Oct. 1st and the balance Oct 16th.<span class='line-break'> </span>Also please send me 100 lbs of salt.</p>
<p>Yours Resp'y<span class='line-break'> </span>J. W. Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span>per F. A. B. </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1063711">
<h3><a name="page-1063711">CB10_0018</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>18</p>
<p>Sept 28    8  [1888]</p>

<p>Yours Resp'y<span class='line-break'> </span>J. W. Lovering Supt<span class='line-break'> </span>per F. A. B.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1063715">CB10_0022</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>22</p>
<p>S</p>
<p>Oct. 1, 1888</p>
<p>Geo. S. Hale, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>Your note is received.  the rent for the deposit of the remains of Noble Maxwell in our tomb is paid until Oct. 15th.</p>
<p>Please sign the enclosed order filling in the day and <span class='line-break'> </span>hour when you wish the removal to take place, and return the order<span class='line-break'> </span>to me giving us at least 24 hours notice.  At the present season the <span class='line-break'> </span>office is open from 8 A.M. until about 5 P.M., but if convenient it<span class='line-break'> </span>would be advisable to make the removal in the forenoon.</p>
<p>If the body is to be removed to a lot in this cemetery<span class='line-break'> </span>the location of the grave in thelot will have to be given before<span class='line-break'></span>hand.  If it is to be removed to another cemetery a permit will<span class='line-break'> </span>have to be obtained from the lerk of the Board of Health of the<span class='line-break'> </span>town of Watertown.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>

<p>I find that you signed the papers for the interment<span class='line-break'> </span>of the late Charles T. Green who was interred in 1872.  Compl<span class='line-break'></span>aint has been made by the proprietor of an adjoining lot that this <span class='line-break'> </span>lot is in rather an unsightly condition, and I have thought that<span class='line-break'> </span>perhaps you might be able to give me the address of the heirs, or <span class='line-break'> </span>of some parties interested.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>#3813 - S</p>
<p>Oct. 10, 1888.</p>
<p>Miss Caroline S. Staples, <span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Madam: -</p>
<p>Regarding the lot in the rear of yours of which you <span class='line-break'> </span>complained of yesterday as being in an unsightly condition, I find<span class='line-break'> </span>that the order for the interment of the late proprietor was signe<span class='line-break'> </span>by Mrs. Jane English #47 Hanover St., Boston, and I have written<span class='line-break'> </span>that lady to see if anything can be done.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<div id="page-1063759">
<h3><a name="page-1063759">CB10_0066</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>66</p>
<p>Oct. 26,  1888.</p>
<p>J. Foster Flagg, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Brooklyn.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>The cost of building a foundation and setting a headstone<span class='line-break'> </span>as per sketch in your letter of 24th will be $6.40, the stones to <span class='line-break'> </span>be delivered in this cemetery.  If the stonecutter does not send<span class='line-break'> </span>dowells with the stone or  prepare the holes to receive them, there <span class='line-break'> </span>will be an extra charge.</p>
<p>We build foundations the exact size of the base stone<span class='line-break'> </span>and down to the lower edge of the grave (5' - 6").  When the foun<span class='line-break'></span>dation is larger than the stone a yellow margin of sod shows around the bse.</p>
<p>Stones coming from New York are usually carried by the <span class='line-break'> </span>Metropolitan S. S. Co. to Boston, and from thence by Express <span class='line-break'> </span>to this place.  There is no freight depot near here, so it is very much<span class='line-break'> </span>better to send direct to Boston.</p>
<p>I enclose you a tracing of the lot showing the location <span class='line-break'> </span>of Mrs. Flagg's grave, please mark on it the exact place on which <span class='line-break'> </span>the stone will stand, and return with your order.</p>
<p>The foundation will be built as soon as the order is <span class='line-break'> </span>received, and the stone set when delivered, if the weather is suit<span class='line-break'></span>able.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<div id="page-1063768">
<h3><a name="page-1063768">CB10_0075</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>75</p>
<p>Nov. 2, 1888.</p>
<p>#2975 - S</p>
<p>Miss Mary T. Bradford,<span class='line-break'> </span>Lancaster, Mass.</p>
<p>Dear Madam: -</p>
<p>Your note is received.  To spade up the lot, enrich<span class='line-break'> </span>with manure, add sufficient loam to fill up the depressions and <span class='line-break'> </span>sow grass seed will cost $25.00</p>
<p>For the same work, but instead of seeding to replace the <span class='line-break'> </span>sod as far as it will go , and furnish the balance needed to resod<span class='line-break'> </span>the lot will cost $35.00.</p>
<p>Both these estimates include the care of the lot for 1889<span class='line-break'> </span>but not the replanting of the myrtle, the understanding being that <span class='line-break'> </span>it will be removed.</p>
<p>Building proper foundations under seven headstones and <span class='line-break'> </span>setting them will cost $34.40.  Our rules require that all stones <span class='line-break'> </span>be set on foundations that are built to the lower edge of the grave <span class='line-break'> </span>(about 5' - 6" ), and our experieince is that a less depth will not <span class='line-break'> </span>make permanent work.</p>
<p>Cleaning all the stone in the lot will cost $10.00</p>
<p>The old fence will pay for its removal, recutting four<span class='line-break'> </span>posts for the corners, removing the other posts and filling up the <span class='line-break'> </span>holes and cutting the number of the lot, provided the work is done <span class='line-break'> </span>at the same time as the grading.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1063769">
<h3><a name="page-1063769">CB10_0076</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>76</p>
<p>#2975-S-2</p>
<p>If the lot is sown with grass seed a permanent sod cannot <span class='line-break'> </span>be had as soon, and the lot would have to be watered by hose for at <span class='line-break'> </span>least two years, so that in the end the charge would be quite as <span class='line-break'> </span>much.</p>
<p>the order for work does not necessarily need to be wri<span class='line-break'></span>tten on our blanks you can write in an orderinary letter your direct<span class='line-break'></span>ions as to the particular work you wish done, and this letter will <span class='line-break'> </span>be your voucher as to price.</p>
<p>I will look into the matter of vases and write you ^later^ [latter crossed out]</p>
<p>Respectfully yours</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1063770">
<h3><a name="page-1063770">CB10_0077</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>77</p>
<p>#1578 - S</p>
<p>Nov. 2, 1888.</p>
<p>W. F. Gavett, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir: <span class='line-break'></span>As it is not usual for contracts to provide for stones <span class='line-break'> </span>not already erected the letter you sent went out in the ordinary<span class='line-break'> </span>course of business, but I find from the contract thta you are right <span class='line-break'> </span>as to the stone just placed being already provided for.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
<p>#1140 - S</p>
<p>Nov.  2,   1888.</p>
<p>C. Amory Stevens, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>New York.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>The foundation can be built as sonn as you desire it.<span class='line-break'> </span>It will soon be too late for that kind of work this Season.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1063771">
<h3><a name="page-1063771">CB10_0078</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>78</p>
<p>#[1939?] - S</p>
<p>Nov. 2, 1888.</p>
<p>Ezra Forristall, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>Your order on the Crosby lot is received and will have <span class='line-break'> </span>attention.  The lot will be resodded, using the present sod as far <span class='line-break'> </span>as it will go and supplying the balance for $30.00</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
<p>#2874 - S</p>
<p>Nov. 2, 1888</p>
<p>Elisha Bassett, Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Newton Centre.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>Your note to our Treasurer has been forwarded to me for <span class='line-break'> </span>answer.  I am sorry that the bill sent you for repairs to the <span class='line-break'> </span>myrtle is not satisfactory.  I have examined the charge, and do not <span class='line-break'> </span>think it is an unfair one.  The charges for repairs to myrtle <span class='line-break'> </span>are more unsatisfactory to both sides than any other class of work we<span class='line-break'> </span>do. If the myrtle is not in good condition in the Spring follow<span class='line-break'></span>ing the repairs we are expected to make it good.  In fairness to <span class='line-break'> </span>the Corporation I do not see that any deduction could be made in <span class='line-break'> </span>your bill, unless you are willing to take the risk of the young<span class='line-break'> </span>myrtle going over the winter, in which case a reduction of $2.50<span class='line-break'> </span>might be made.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>Respectfully yours,<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>

<p>Simson E. Baldwin, Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>New Haven, Conn.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>Your note is received, enclosing $2.00 and requesting<span class='line-break'> </span>a report and opinion on the inscription just cut on the Marett<span class='line-break'> </span>monument. A receipt for the amount is herewith enclosed. The<span class='line-break'> </span>inscription is as given below, except that the name Martha B.<span class='line-break'> </span>Marett is cut in a semi-circle to conform to the moulding of the<span class='line-break'> </span>die and to the other inscription.</p>
<p>The workmanship is fair.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt<span class='line-break'> </span>MARTHA B. MARETT<span class='line-break'> </span>DAUGHTER OF<span class='line-break'> </span>JOSIAH KNAPP,<span class='line-break'> </span>WIDOW OF<span class='line-break'> </span>PHILIP MARETT<span class='line-break'> </span>DIED SEPT. 2, 1878<span class='line-break'> </span>AGED 82 YEARS</p>

<p>Messrs H.P. Smith &amp; Co.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sirs:-</p>
<p>At the present time we cannot promise foundations less<span class='line-break'> </span>than a week from the time we are notified by the Treasurer to go on<span class='line-break'> </span>with the work, but if these are in a hurry we will try and push<span class='line-break'> </span>them ahead.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
<p>#2975-S</p>
<p>Nov. 15, 1888.</p>

<p>Dear Madam:-</p>
<p>Your note is received, the lot will have the ordinary <span class='line-break'> </span>care in 1889, but we never guarantee sod where part is old sod<span class='line-break'> </span>removed and relaid. As I desire this matter to be clear I will<span class='line-break'> </span>wait until I hear from you before going on with the work.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1063803">CB10_0101</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when=''>1888-11-14</date></p>
<p>101<span class='line-break'> </span>#599-S</p>
<p>Nov. 14, 1888.</p>
<p>Miss Anna L. Shaw,<span class='line-break'> </span>#121 Charles St., Boston</p>
<p>Dear Madam: -</p>
<p>I find that the base of the monument on your lot has <span class='line-break'> </span>not been cleaned for some time, and while it cannot be made as <span class='line-break'> </span>good as new it can be very much improved.  The charge for cleaning<span class='line-break'> </span>will be $5.00</p>
<p>I notice that there is an unpaid bill on this lot, which <span class='line-break'> </span>I enclose, as the Trustees do not permit me to do any work on lots<span class='line-break'> </span>where there are back bills, this will have to be paid before any<span class='line-break'></span>thing is done.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>2364. Munroe.</p>
<p>Setting headstone 2 00</p>
<p>PAYABLE IN ADVANCE</p>

<p>S</p>
<p>Nov. 16, 1888.</p>
<p>Highland Slate Mnf. Co.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sirs:-</p>
<p>The nearest freight depot is Union Market on the P.R.R.<span class='line-break'> </span>There there are private side tracks the charge is too high to make<span class='line-break'> </span>them available. Our experience is that it is cheaper to team out<span class='line-break'> </span>direct from Boston.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>

<p><date when=''>1888-11-17</date></p>
<p>110</p>
<p>#4144-S</p>
<p>Messrs Miller &amp; Luce,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sirs:-</p>
<p>Your note is received, you will require a permit from<span class='line-break'> </span>the proprietor before delivering the stones. At the request of the<span class='line-break'> </span>N.E. Mont. Co. we forwarded Sept. 19th, to Mrs L Pierpont Crosby<span class='line-break'> </span>#3 Chauncy St., Boston the necessary paper for her signature.</p>

<p>November 19, [188]8</p>
<p>H.B. Mackintosh Treas.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: --</p>
<p>I do not quite<span class='line-break'> </span>understand the enclosed order. The<span class='line-break'> </span>price for care of the three lots is<span class='line-break'> </span>$6.00 ($3.00 -- $1.50 + $1.50), therefore the<span class='line-break'> </span>top dressing would be $4.00. Is the<span class='line-break'> </span>top-dressing to be put on this year?</p>
<p>Yours Resp'y.</p>

<div id="page-1063826">
<h3><a name="page-1063826">CB10_0111</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>111</p>
<p>Nov. 17, 1888.</p>
<p>Messrs Evans &amp; Tombs.<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sirs: -</p>
<p>As a difficulty which can easily be obviated has been <span class='line-break'> </span>found in setting some of the headstones you have been sending here,<span class='line-break'> </span>I desire to call your attention to it believing you will consider <span class='line-break'> </span>it for your interest to remedy it in future, and thereby give those <span class='line-break'> </span>who employ you a more substantial piece of work with probably no <span class='line-break'> </span>increase of expense.</p>
<p>The stones in question have come with a rough socket base <span class='line-break'> </span>as indicated in the sketch, the tablet being cut so that this base <span class='line-break'> </span>cannot be set more than 3 or 4 inches below sod.  The result is a <span class='line-break'> </span>yellow margin of dead sod around the stone from the want of soil.<span class='line-break'> </span>These bases ought to be at least one foot under the sod, and it <span class='line-break'> </span>would be very much better and probably might curtail the expense <span class='line-break'> </span>[?] foundation by reducing its size, if the base stone was dis<span class='line-break'></span>pensed with altogether, and the tablet made long enough and built <span class='line-break'> </span>into the foundation, which should be covered by at least twelve <span class='line-break'> </span>inches of soil.</p>
<p>As the Corporation has in many cases ageed to keep the<span class='line-break'> </span>grass in perpetual care, it is necessary that the stones be so <span class='line-break'> </span>designed that this is possible.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,  J. W. Lovering Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1063828">
<h3><a name="page-1063828">CB10_0112</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>112</p>
<p>November 19/88</p>
<p>Mrs. J. E. Neale.</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>The gardener has<span class='line-break'> </span>looked at the ivy on your lot #3225<span class='line-break'> </span>and says he does not think he can make<span class='line-break'> </span>it grow outside in the winter as they<span class='line-break'> </span>are not at all hardy. Yours Resp'y<span class='line-break'> </span>J. W. Lovering Sup't.<span class='line-break'> </span>per F. A. B.</p>
<p>#2178-S<span class='line-break'> </span>Nov. 20, 1888.</p>
<p>Genl J. F. Head,</p>
<p>Washington D. C.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>The enclosed bill has been forwarded to me by our<span class='line-break'> </span>Treasurer with the request to send you an explanation as to the<span class='line-break'> </span>plants charged. These plants were ordered for this year only, by<span class='line-break'> </span>a lady who came here I think to inspect a monument, the order on<span class='line-break'> </span>file here was signed for you by Col A. A. Rand of Boston.</p>
<p>There is no order for topdressing, nor is it charged in<span class='line-break'> </span>this bill. Am I to understand your note as ordering it now?</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>

<p>Nov. 20, 1888.</p>
<p>A. Klaber, Esq.</p>
<p>#238 E 57th St., New York.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>Your note is received, there are several Magoun lots in<span class='line-break'> </span>this cemetery and I do not know to which you refer. If you do not<span class='line-break'> </span>know the number of the lot tell me the name of the person at whose<span class='line-break'> </span>grave the stone is placed, and I can trace it.</p>
<p>When not ordered by the proprietor these bills are pay<span class='line-break'></span>able in advance. The cost of these two foundations will be $17.80.<span class='line-break'> </span>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>#1391-S</p>

<p>#1792-S</p>
<p>Nov. 24, 1888.</p>
<p>Mrs. Eugene Delano,</p>
<p>Philadelphia.</p>
<p>Dear Mada:</p>
<p>Your note is received. It will be better to have all<span class='line-break'> </span>the woek done next Spring, if we were to raise the grave of the<span class='line-break'> </span>late Re. Dr. Adams we could not sod it properly on account of<span class='line-break'> </span>frost.</p>
<p>The chares for the years 1886, 1887 and 1888 were $8.00<span class='line-break'> </span>each year for the care fo the lot, which includes cutting the<span class='line-break'> </span>grass and keeping the lot tidy.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>

<h3><a name="page-1063837">CB10_0116</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>116</p>
<p>#1793-S</p>
<p>Nov. 24, 1888.</p>
<p>A. Kraber, Esq.,</p>
<p>New York.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:</p>
<p>A great many of the granite underbases are made in Quincy<span class='line-break'> </span>and sent here. I would not care to recommend any particular stone<span class='line-break'></span>cuter; but I have no doubt you know several out there.</p>
<p>Bearly all the stones are set in this cemetery by the<span class='line-break'> </span>workmen of the Corporation, if you will send me a tracing of the <span class='line-break'> </span>stone I will send you estimate.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
<p>#1878-S</p>

<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>The grade as proposed for the Simonds lot #3757 would <span class='line-break'> </span>not admit of front steps.  The rear would be kept substantially <span class='line-break'> </span>as now and the grade rise to the front (East) two inches per foot, and<span class='line-break'> </span>from left to right (South to North) would fall three fourths of an <span class='line-break'> </span>inch per foot.  As you will notrice there is considerable fall from <span class='line-break'> </span>front to rear which would be bad for a monument of any great width <span class='line-break'> </span>and as the lot is only about 16 feet long a narrow monument would <span class='line-break'> </span>give more graves.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>

<div id="page-1063915">
<h3><a name="page-1063915">CB10_0152</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>152</p>
<p>#1662-S</p>
<p>Dec. 22 1888.</p>
<p>Mrs. Mary S. Hawley,<span class='line-break'> </span>Waltham</p>
<p>Dear Madam: -</p>
<p>Your note of 17th has been forwarded to me by our <span class='line-break'> </span>Treasurer for answer.</p>
<p>The sum needed for the perpetual care of lot #1662 incl<span class='line-break'></span>uding six myrtle graves, and the cleaning and renewal of the sar<span class='line-break'></span>cophagus and four headstones, will be $700.00.  If the cleaning <span class='line-break'> </span>only and not the renewal is included, he sum needed will be <span class='line-break'> </span>$500.00, and if the myrtle is removed from the lot the sum needed <span class='line-break'> </span>will be $150.00 less.</p>
<p>The perpetual care of a lot includes more than the care <span class='line-break'> </span>and occasional topdressing you pay for annually.  Lots under  per<span class='line-break'></span>petual care contracts are likely to have much better care, and are <span class='line-break'> </span>topdressed oftener.  In the contracts for perpetal care are inc<span class='line-break'></span>luded many small repairs to the sod, and even the entire resodding,<span class='line-break'> </span>of the lot, if needed, which are items of extra expense in addition <span class='line-break'> </span>to the usual annual charges.  Th perpetual care contract is for <span class='line-break'> </span>all time, and under it the corporation assumes the risk of the <span class='line-break'> </span>cost of labor, materials and the rate of interest hereafter.  If <span class='line-break'> </span>you desire to assume this risk, a donation of say $300.00 could <span class='line-break'> </span>be made, and the corporation will keep the principal whole and</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1063917">
<h3><a name="page-1063917">CB10_0153</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>153</p>
<p>#1662-S-2</p>
<p>expend the interest on the lot as far as it will go, but our ex<span class='line-break'></span>perience is that the lot will require the sum named in the first <span class='line-break'> </span>estimate to keep it in such repair as other lots now under per<span class='line-break'></span>petual care are kept.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1063919">
<h3><a name="page-1063919">CB10_0154</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>154</p>
<p>#1956-S</p>
<p>Dec. 24, 1888.</p>
<p>W. T. Piper, Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Cambridge</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>I have looked up the matter of the location of the head<span class='line-break'></span>stones in regard to which you called.  I find that the headstone <span class='line-break'> </span>of the late Mrs. Mary E. Piper is not exactly over its foundation.<span class='line-break'> </span>If it is moved so that the space between it and that of Solomon <span class='line-break'> </span>Piper will be the same as between that and the one of Jerusha Piper <span class='line-break'> </span>it will then be practically ovr its foundation.  It appears that <span class='line-break'> </span>in planting the myrtle we did not place it exactly over the grave <span class='line-break'> </span>of Mrs. Mary E. Piper, and if you will have the stone moved to its<span class='line-break'> </span>new position, will have have the myrtle replanted so as to centre on <span class='line-break'> </span>it as soon as such work can be done in the Spring.</p>
<p>The gardener reports that he covered the myrtle on the <span class='line-break'> </span>graves of Solomon Piper and Jerusha Piper, but that he now finds<span class='line-break'> </span>it uncovered.  The covering will be replaced.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>

<p>Dec. 27, 1888.</p>
<p>Chas. G. Gibson, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>I wrote you Dec. 11th in regard to the marker for Mr. <span class='line-break'> </span>Blanchards lot, but write again as I fear the note has been mis<span class='line-break'></span>sent, and it would be well to have the work attended to while this <span class='line-break'> </span>weather lasts.  The marker requires a foundation under it, and I <span class='line-break'> </span>understood you wished it placed at the end of the grave nearest <span class='line-break'> </span>the path, but as a space has been left at the other end, where <span class='line-break'> </span>stones are usually placed it would be economy of space to place<span class='line-break'> </span>this one there.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>An addition of 70 sq. ft., that is a strip about five <span class='line-break'> </span>ft. wide, could be sold for interment purposes, or for placing a <span class='line-break'> </span>monument, this is the land in which the flower beds are now cut.<span class='line-break'> </span>The banks could not be carried out further on account of the ad<span class='line-break'></span>joining lots, but the lot and addition can be regraded at the same <span class='line-break'> </span>grade as now. <p>In regard to the addition you desire to your lot, I <span class='line-break'> </span>find that if the fence is to remain there is only  room enough to <span class='line-break'> </span>pass between the lots, and an addition could not be sold.  If the <span class='line-break'> </span>fence is to come away it is barely possible that an addition large <span class='line-break'> </span>enough for one grave could be sold.</p>
<p>To paint the fence two coats black paint will cost $12.00<span class='line-break'> </span>or one coat of asphaltum $8.00. <p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>

<p>#1518-S</p>
<p>Jan. 12, 1889.</p>
<p>S. P. Jones, Esq.,</p>
<p>#47 Woodbine St., Roxbury.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>The fence on the lot standing in the name of the heirs <span class='line-break'> </span>of James L. Jones is in a rusty and unsightly condition, and the <span class='line-break'> </span>lot and its surroundings would be improved by removing it.  Will <span class='line-break'> </span>you authorize me to do this recut the posts at the corners, fill <span class='line-break'> </span>up and sod over the other post holes and cut the number of the lot,<span class='line-break'> </span>without expense to you except the old material.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1063979">CB10_0182</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>[?page?] 182<span class='line-break'> </span>[column1]<span class='line-break'> </span>January 15th<span class='line-break'> </span>4<span class='line-break'> </span>9.<span class='line-break'> </span>Honorable [?Henry?] H. [?Gil????],<span class='line-break'> </span>[???fing?]<span class='line-break'> </span>Your note of<span class='line-break'> </span>yesterday in regards to fast driving <span class='line-break'> </span>from the Cemetery is received and <span class='line-break'> </span>will have careful attention.</p>
<p>From the particulars which <span class='line-break'> </span>you have given me, I have been <span class='line-break'> </span>able to ascertain the person at <span class='line-break'> </span>fault, and shall take such <span class='line-break'> </span>steps as will, I trust prevent any <span class='line-break'> </span>such accident in the future.<span class='line-break'> </span>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>J. W. Lovering</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Superintendant<span class='line-break'> </span>[/column1]</p>
<p>[column2]<span class='line-break'> </span>January 15<span class='line-break'> </span>9.<span class='line-break'> </span>Messrs. <a href='/pages/subjects/25009327' title='Mr. Lewis'>Lewis</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/25009328' title='Mr. Jones'>Jones</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/25009329' title='Mr. Ton'>Ton</a>, <span class='line-break'> </span>Dear Sirs, <span class='line-break'> </span>Complaint has <span class='line-break'> </span>been made by the City of  <span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/53203' title='Cambridge, MA'>Cambridge</a> that on last Sunday <span class='line-break'> </span>afternoon a hearse was driven so <span class='line-break'> </span>rapidly through the front gate, by <span class='line-break'> </span>one of your drivers, that only with <span class='line-break'> </span>great difficulty was a collision <span class='line-break'> </span>avoided with a vehicle passing.</p>
<p>I trust it will be only necessary <span class='line-break'> </span>to call your attention to the matter, <span class='line-break'> </span>and to the rules of the Cemetery which <span class='line-break'> </span>forbid fast driving within it, to <span class='line-break'> </span>prevent any thing of the kind in the future. <span class='line-break'> </span>Yours truly, <span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>J. W. Lovering</a> <span class='line-break'> </span>Superintendant<span class='line-break'> </span>[/column2]</p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1063981">CB10_0183</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>183</p>
<p>Jan'y 15 [188]9</p>
<p>Messrs Lewis Jones [&amp;Son?}</p>
<p>Dear Sir:</p>
<p>Complaint has <span class='line-break'> </span>been made by the City of <span class='line-break'> </span>Cambridge that on last Sunday <span class='line-break'> </span>afternoon a hearse was driven so <span class='line-break'> </span>rapidly through the front gate by <span class='line-break'> </span>one of your drivers, that only with <span class='line-break'> </span>great difficulty was a collision <span class='line-break'> </span>avoided with a vehicle passing.</p>
<p>I trust it will be ony necessary <span class='line-break'> </span>to call your attention to the matter <span class='line-break'> </span>and to the rules of the Cemetery which <span class='line-break'> </span>forbid fast driving wihtin it, to <span class='line-break'> </span>prevent any thing of the kind in the future.</p>
<p>Yrs truly - J. W. Lovering</p>

<div id="page-1063985">
<h3><a name="page-1063985">CB10_0185</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>185</p>
<p>January 15 [188]9</p>
<p>G. W. Wilson Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston Museum</p>
<p>Dear Sir:</p>
<p>Yours received in<span class='line-break'> </span>reference to plants to be set on <span class='line-break'> </span>the new made grave in lot 4777.<span class='line-break'> </span>Violets remain in blossom for a <span class='line-break'> </span>short time only in the spring of <span class='line-break'> </span>the year.  The Gardener suggests <span class='line-break'> </span>either Lobelia or dwarf Aguratum<span class='line-break'> </span>each being of a purplish blue color <span class='line-break'> </span>and remaining in blossom for a<span class='line-break'> </span>longer period than the Violet.</p>
<p>the former order has been for <span class='line-break'> </span>four (4.00) dollars worth on two</p>
<p>pg. 2</p>
<p>graves and three dollars ($3.00) worth<span class='line-break'> </span>in border.  Will you kindly make<span class='line-break'> </span>out new order on enclosed card<span class='line-break'> </span>that I may understand if you <span class='line-break'> </span>wish the amount of plants in<span class='line-break'></span>creased or the four dollars worth<span class='line-break'> </span>consisting of two and two thirds ( 2/3)<span class='line-break'> </span>dozen to cover the three graves also<span class='line-break'> </span>if the same amount of mixed<span class='line-break'> </span>plants as formerly are to be placed <span class='line-break'> </span>in the border.  By so doing <span class='line-break'> </span>you will oblige.</p>
<p>Ours Resp'y.<span class='line-break'> </span>J. W. Lovering Sup't.<span class='line-break'> </span>per F. A. B. <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1063987">
<h3><a name="page-1063987">CB10_0186</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>186</p>
<p>Jan. 16, 1889.</p>
<p>John R. Scofield, Esq.,</p>
<p>Supt. Woodlawn Cem., Stamford, Conn.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>The remains can be received here at any time, and the <span class='line-break'> </span>brick grave prepared for them.  The cost of a brick grave is $23.00<span class='line-break'> </span>for a person over ten years of age.  It would be well if we had <span class='line-break'> </span>48 hours notice of the hour of interment, and the size of the box<span class='line-break'> </span>so that we may know how large to build the grave.  We have no <span class='line-break'> </span>facilities for going outside the cemetery to receive a body, but <span class='line-break'> </span>if the remains come by express they will be delivered here, other<span class='line-break'></span>wise you will have to get some Boston undertaker to receive the <span class='line-break'> </span>body and convey it to this cemetery.</p>
<p>Please have the enclosed order signed by the proprietor <span class='line-break'> </span>and the blanks filled out (the proprietor of the lot in this cem<span class='line-break'></span>etery I mean).  Our State law requires a permit from the Board of <span class='line-break'> </span>Health, or Selectmen of the town from whence the remains are to be <span class='line-break'> </span>removed, this had better be glued to the box and a duplicate mailed<span class='line-break'> </span>to me.</p>
<p>I am sorry that our rules are out of print at present.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<div class="page-content">
<p>188</p>
<p>#793-S</p>
<p>Jan. 17. 1889.</p>
<p>Mrs. Alpheus Hardy,</p>
<p>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Madam: -</p>
<p>I find that to repair the name plate on the fence of <span class='line-break'> </span>the Rogers lot will cost not over $5.00.  The fund deposited for <span class='line-break'> </span>the care of this lot is smaller than usual, and the interest of it <span class='line-break'> </span>for the coming year will not be enough to give the lot such care <span class='line-break'> </span>as it usually has had and also make this repair to the fence.<span class='line-break'> </span>I will be glad to follow the wishes of the proprietors of the lot <span class='line-break'> </span>in the matter, by either repairing the plate at their expense, or <span class='line-break'> </span>omitting some part of the care for the coming year and making the <span class='line-break'> </span>repair at the expense of the fund.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1063994">
<h3><a name="page-1063994">CB10_0189</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>189</p>
<p>#2538-S</p>
<p>Jan. 17. 1889</p>
<p>F. E. Davidson, Esq.,</p>
<p>c/o Baring Bros &amp; Co.<span class='line-break'> </span>London, England.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>Your note is received.  The fence on the lot might be <span class='line-break'> </span>repaired but the expense would be considerable, and as it is rusty <span class='line-break'> </span>and unsightly the appearance of the lot and its surroundings would <span class='line-break'> </span>be improved, and the constant expense of painting avoided by remov<span class='line-break'></span>ing it as very many of our proprietors have done with the fences <span class='line-break'> </span>on their lots.  To do this, remove all the posts but four at the <span class='line-break'> </span>corners, recut those and cut the number of the lot on one of them,<span class='line-break'> </span>fill up and sod over the other post holes, raise a sunken grave and <span class='line-break'> </span>build a foundation under a headstone now out of plumb, with the <span class='line-break'> </span>care of the lot for the year 1889 would cost $10.00 and the old <span class='line-break'> </span>material of the fence.</p>
<p>The care of the lot without plants or topdressing would <span class='line-break'> </span>cost $2.00 a year, as you are abroad I would suggest that an order<span class='line-break'> </span>for the care of the lot until countermanded would keep the grass <span class='line-break'> </span>cut and the lot clean and tidy.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<div class="page-content">
<p><date when=''>1889-01-18</date></p>
<p>191</p>
<p>Jan'y 18th [188]9.</p>
<p>C.U. Cotting Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The Thorndike lot<span class='line-break'> </span>appears to me to be in as good condi<span class='line-break'></span>tion as could be expected at this season<span class='line-break'> </span>of the year. The adjoining lot has<span class='line-break'> </span>been top dressed with manure, but<span class='line-break'> </span>the Thorndike lot, as well as all other<span class='line-break'> </span>lots under perpetual care has received<span class='line-break'> </span>two top dressings with fertilizer, which<span class='line-break'> </span>is considered as on the whole more<span class='line-break'> </span>satisfactory &amp; much neater. If,<span class='line-break'> </span>however, it would be more satisfactory<span class='line-break'> </span>to the owners to have manure used, I<span class='line-break'> </span>can have some put on.</p>
<p>Yrs truly</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1064002">CB10_0193</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when=''>1889-01-18</date></p>
<p>193</p>
<p>#1000-S</p>
<p>Jan. 18, 1889.</p>
<p>Mrs. H.M.H. Currier,<span class='line-break'> </span>Jamaica Plain.</p>
<p>Dear Madam:-</p>
<p>In regard to the enclosed bill, you will remember that<span class='line-break'> </span>in my conversation with you last Summer I said that the myrtle<span class='line-break'> </span>removed from your lot was old and not such as I cared to buy. I<span class='line-break'> </span>have since consulted with the gardener, and find that it is with<span class='line-break'></span>out any any value to us.</p>
<p>The charge for the work was clearly agreed upon. In one<span class='line-break'> </span>case it was to be $37.00 and the old myrtle, in the other $3.00<span class='line-break'> </span>the myrtle to be at your disposal if called for in the Fall. The<span class='line-break'> </span>myrtle is at your disposal now, but we cannot agree to keep it<span class='line-break'> </span>beyond May 1st, as our room is very limited.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>The original corner posts on your lot were removed and<span class='line-break'> </span>moulded posts set in place of them, but on these the number of the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot was not cut as required by our bye-laws. <p>Supt.</p>

<p>197</p>
<p>#2746-S</p>
<p>Jan. 21, 1889.</p>
<p>S.A. Denio, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>The sum needed for the perpetual care of your lot, inclu<span class='line-break'></span>ding the sod and the cleaning but not the renewal of the monument<span class='line-break'> </span>and without plants or myrtle will be $350.00. For the two myrtle<span class='line-break'> </span>graves $50.00 will be needed, and if the cleaning but not the re<span class='line-break'></span>newal of the two marble headstones is included $50.00 more will be<span class='line-break'> </span>required. If you propose to have the usual quantity of plants in<span class='line-break'> </span>the North border only, an additional sum of $100.00 will be needed,<span class='line-break'> </span>or if you wish to have the usual number of plants in the North and<span class='line-break'> </span>East borders, that is the border on Eagle ave. as well as that on<span class='line-break'> </span>Spruce ave., the additional amount needed will be $200.00. This<span class='line-break'> </span>provides for the amount of mixed plants that are usually set in<span class='line-break'> </span>such borders, but of course the planting can be made more elaborate<span class='line-break'> </span>if you care to go to the expense.</p>
<p>To recapitulate, the amounts are as under:</p>
<p><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>Perpetual care of grass and cleaning of monument</th> <th>$350.00<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>Two myrtle graves</td> <td>50.00</td> </tr> <tr><td>Cleaning two Marble headstones</td> <td>50.00</td> </tr> <tr><td>Usual plants in Spruce ave. border</td> <td>100.00</td> </tr> <tr><td>Usual plants in Eagle ave. border (if wanted)</td> <td><u>100.00</u></td> </tr> <tr><td/> <td>$650.00</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1064015">
<h3><a name="page-1064015">CB10_0199</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when=''>1889-01-23</date></p>
<p>199</p>
<p>#4395-S</p>
<p>Jan. 23, 1889.</p>
<p>Messrs Wight &amp; Scorgie,<span class='line-break'> </span>Cambridge.</p>
<p>Dear Sirs:-</p>
<p>In regard to your enquiry as to the Hon. H.H. Gilmore's<span class='line-break'> </span>lot, I find that the distance from the lot line to the line of the<span class='line-break'> </span>path must not exceed five feet. The rise from the path to the lot<span class='line-break'> </span>will not be over nine inches. The width of the front of the lot<span class='line-break'> </span>is twelve feet, and I need hardly remind you that the extreme width<span class='line-break'> </span>of the entrance posts, steps and buttresses must not exceed half<span class='line-break'> </span>that width, that is six feet, and that border stones are not per<span class='line-break'></span>missible. The depth of the underground roots of the corner posts<span class='line-break'> </span>should not be less than five feet. A post that only goes below<span class='line-break'> </span>the frost line is not considered of proper depth, as graves are<span class='line-break'> </span>made close to these posts and any sinking of the grave is followed<span class='line-break'> </span>by the tipping of the post, unless it reaches as far as the<span class='line-break'> </span>bottom of the grave.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
<p>I would say that the lot line above referred to is the<span class='line-break'> </span><u>inside line</u> of the present posts.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<div id="page-1064043">
<h3><a name="page-1064043">CB10_0212</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when=''>1889-02-01</date></p>
<p>212</p>
<p>#2746-S</p>
<p>Feb. 1, 1889.</p>
<p>S.A. Denio, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>Your note is received. I have no doubt that the salvia<span class='line-break'> </span>is the plant you have in mind, as there are a large number of them<span class='line-break'> </span>used in the cemetery. It is not a shrub however, but an annual<span class='line-break'> </span>plant that has to be set out each year. As it only blooms a<span class='line-break'> </span>portion of the season, I hardly think that you would be satisfied<span class='line-break'> </span>with that alone, and our practice is to set it out with a variety<span class='line-break'> </span>of mixed plants so that there may be a continuation of blooms thr[sic]-<span class='line-break'> </span>ought the season. Under ordinary circumstances if the contract<span class='line-break'> </span>was made for plants in the Spruce avenue border only, there would<span class='line-break'> </span>be from two to four salvias set out with the other plants, but of<span class='line-break'> </span>course if you desired more of it your wish would be attended to<span class='line-break'> </span>whenever the plant could be got. I am sorry that being only an<span class='line-break'> </span>annual plant there is none of it to be seen here at present.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<p>213</p>
<p>#2052-S</p>
<p>Feb. 1, 1889.</p>
<p>Mrs. L.M. Chamberlain,<span class='line-break'> </span>Newton Centre, Mass.</p>

The charge for the use of two<span class='line-break'> </span>hydrangeas in 1887 was $3.00, in 1888 large and handsome plants<span class='line-break'> </span>were asked for, and the charge was made $5.00. As there was no<span class='line-break'> </span>special notification of the change given you I will make the charge<span class='line-break'> </span>$3.00 as before, but as there is a large expense attending the care<span class='line-break'> </span>and watering of these plants, such plants as you had last year<span class='line-break'> </span>cannot hereafter be charged at less than $5.00.</p>

<div id="page-1064055">
<h3><a name="page-1064055">CB10_0218</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when=''>1889-02-06</date></p>
<p>#2746-S</p>
<p>Feb. 6, 1889.</p>
<p>S.A. Denio, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>Your note of 4th is received. Our practice is to make<span class='line-break'> </span>removals of remains only on the order of the proprietor of the lot.<span class='line-break'> </span>In case of a dispute we would probably refuse to recognize any one<span class='line-break'> </span>except the owner, unless ordered by the courts.</p>
<p>I do not know of any decision of the courts that it<span class='line-break'> </span>would be safe to make a general statement from.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<h3><a name="page-1064062">CB10_0221</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when=''>1889-02-06</date></p>
<p>221</p>
<p>#2443)S</p>
<p>Feb. 6, 1889.</p>
<p>H.D. Litchfield, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Cambridge.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>In regard to your proposed removal of the remains of a<span class='line-break'> </span>child from tomb #2443, as you are aware the lot was reconveyed in<span class='line-break'> </span>trust to the Corporation, and by my copy of the deed the removal<span class='line-break'> </span>of the bodies now in the tomb is not provided for. In view of<span class='line-break'> </span>that I do not see that I have any authority to make a removal.</p>
<p>I suppose if the heirs and executor unite in asking <span class='line-break'> </span>for a modification of the deed it might be made, but as the contr<span class='line-break'></span>act is made with our Trustees the change would have to be approved<span class='line-break'> </span>by them.</p>
<p>There is a meeting of the Trustees next Wednesday, and it<span class='line-break'> </span>might save you some delay if the papers were sent me before that<span class='line-break'> </span>time.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<p>222</p>
<p>Feby 7. [188]9</p>
<p>Joshua D. Ball</p>
<p>34<span class='line-break'> </span>Bethia Cole<span class='line-break'> </span>Feby 1. [188]9 July 1 [188]9 15 00</p>

<div id="page-1064066">
<h3><a name="page-1064066">CB10_0223</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when=''>1889-02-09</date></p>
<p>223</p>
<p>S</p>
<p>Feb. 9. 1889.</p>
<p>W.F. Primrose, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Sec. Loudon Park Cemetery,<span class='line-break'> </span>Baltimore, Md.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>Your note of 6th inst. is received. The tombs referred<span class='line-break'> </span>to in our annual report are the single compartment tombs with a<span class='line-break'> </span>door above ground where several bodies are placed in this single<span class='line-break'> </span>compartment, in distinction to those in which each body is placed<span class='line-break'> </span>in a separate sealed compartment.</p>
<p>Brick graves and underground tombs being covered with<span class='line-break'> </span>earth are not objected to, and the present rule in this cemetery<span class='line-break'> </span>is, that all tombs that may be built with a door above ground are<span class='line-break'> </span>required to be so constructed that each body is placed in a sepa<span class='line-break'></span>rate compartment, which is hermetically sealed <u>at the time of the</u><span class='line-break'> </span><u>interment</u>. The box tombs, as they are called having only one door<span class='line-break'> </span>between the decaying remains and the outer air, give off odors, and<span class='line-break'> </span>are not considered by health authorities to be proper places for<span class='line-break'> </span>the deposit of the dead.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1064068">

<div class="page-content">
<p><date when=''>1889-02-19</date></p>
<p>225</p>
<p>#2746-S</p>
<p>Feb. 19, 1889.</p>
<p>S.A. Denio, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>Your note is received. If you wish to have perennial<span class='line-break'> </span>shrubs set out, I should think two hydrangeas or two deutzias<span class='line-break'> </span>might answer. If annual plants were wanted the beds might be fill<span class='line-break'></span>ed with a variety of mixed plants so as to ensure a succession of<span class='line-break'> </span>blooms throughout the season.</p>
<p>I am usually at this office every week day except Sat<span class='line-break'></span>urday, but I will probably be away during the end of this week.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1064094">CB10_0236</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>236</p>
<p>March 1, 9</p>
<p>Mrs Evans &amp; Lambs</p>
<p>4412 Foots</p>
<p>Removing two stones to [D?]<u> 3 50</u></p>

<p># 4412-S<span class='line-break'> </span>March  1,  1889.<span class='line-break'> </span>Mesars. Evans &amp; Tombs,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1064120">CB10_0248</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>( 248 )</p>
<p><date when='1889-03-07'>March 7, 1889.</date></p>
<p>Wm. Salway, Esq.,</p>
<p>Supt. Spring Grove Cemetry,</p>
<p>Cincinnette O.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:</p>
<p>Your note is received.  The price of lots in this cem<span class='line-break'></span>etery is from $2.25 to $ 2.75 per foot, but some lots that are<span class='line-break'> </span>exceptionally situated are sold at lower and higher rates.<span class='line-break'> </span>price is for the lot all prepred, marked at the coners with gran<span class='line-break'></span>ite post set level with the sod and numbers, and the perpetual<span class='line-break'> </span>care of the lot is included,</p>
<p>As the lots are all sold under perpetual care it has <span class='line-break'> </span>this year been decided to sell no more singles graves except with<span class='line-break'> </span>a provision for their perpetual care, so they are new sold at the <span class='line-break'> </span>uniform rate of $ 25.00, and if a second interment is made $ 10.00<span class='line-break'> </span>more and the interments fee ($ 5.00 )  in addition in each case. No<span class='line-break'> </span>more than two interments are permitted in the grave, nor is any<span class='line-break'> </span>distinction made except as to the interment fee whether for an <span class='line-break'> </span>adult or for a child.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<h3><a name="page-1064122">CB10_0249</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>249</p>
<p># 3405-S</p>
<p><date when='1889-03-07'>March 7, 1889.</date></p>
<p>Wm. A Everett,  Esq.,</p>
<p>Cambridge.</p>
<p>Dear Sr :-</p>
<p>Your note is received. Marble is the material most <span class='line-break'> </span>tensively used for headstone, <span class='line-break'> </span>better class of granites.</p>
<p>The foundation should not be built or the stone set until<span class='line-break'> </span>the danger from frost is past.</p>
<p>The underground foundation is prepared by our workmen,<span class='line-break'> </span>and where the Corporation has become responsible for the lot thr<span class='line-break'></span>ough its being under perpetual care, they also set the stone. The<span class='line-break'> </span>order for the foundation with the exact loaction in which it is to<span class='line-break'> </span>be built should be sent to this office two or three weeks before<span class='line-break'> </span>the stone is ready to set.</p>
<p>If you will fillout and sign the enclosed blank and for<span class='line-break'></span>ward it to our Sec'y (#5 Pemberton Sq., Boston) he will issue the <span class='line-break'> </span>permit needed for the stonecutter, and will also send you the card<span class='line-break'> </span>of addnission to cemetery.</p>
<p>I enclose you a copy of the latest map issued.</p>
<p>Respectfully your,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>

<p># 3799 -S<span class='line-break'> </span>March 9, 1889.<span class='line-break'> </span>H. H. Hunnewell, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir : -<span class='line-break'> </span>I find from an examination of the curbing on your lot<span class='line-break'> </span># 3799 that to put it in proper repair, the outer stones of the <span class='line-break'> </span>wings of the tomb will have to be reset, some of the curibings reset<span class='line-break'> </span>substanially all the joints releaded and secured with clamps, with<span class='line-break'> </span>special tie rod to clamp the stone of the left hand wing.  This <span class='line-break'> </span>would cost including replacing the sodding in as good condition as<span class='line-break'> </span>new, $ 125.00.<span class='line-break'> </span>Regarding the closing of the door for the Winter, the <span class='line-break'> </span>marble deer might be tapped and brass wire netting with brass <span class='line-break'> </span>rim put on, or a hardwood frame with a glass plate, the bolts to<span class='line-break'> </span>have heads similar to these now keeping the belts and hinges in<span class='line-break'> </span>pleace.  Marble is not a speciall satisfactory material for a tomb<span class='line-break'> </span>door, because of its liability to sag and break.  The doors now<span class='line-break'> </span>generally used are of bronze or other metal,  to the back of which<span class='line-break'> </span>a metal plate can be secured for the Winter months.<span class='line-break'> </span>Cementing the walls of the vestibule is a very is a very unsatis<span class='line-break'></span>factory method.  The cement begins to crack and peel off almost as<span class='line-break'> </span>soon as put on,  so that it never looks rightly.  The cement now or <span class='line-break'> </span>the walls could be all cleared off. the [-----?] [------?] [grade?] as [--------?]</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1064128">
<h3><a name="page-1064128">CB10_0252</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>#3799 #2</p>
<p>its present condition will admit and whitewashed at an expense of $20.00.<span class='line-break'> </span>To finish the vestibule in a way that would be satisfac-tory and lasting, the side and front brick walls and arch should be entirely removed and resconstructed with an air space, a rabbet cut in the capztone to overlap the brick and the whole covered with a coat of asphaltum.<span class='line-break'> </span>If the interior finish were face brick the cost would be about $750.00.<span class='line-break'> </span>Puff brick make a handsomer finish, the cost of that would be about $950.00.</p>
<p>The cost of an underground foundation for a monument with a base 5' - 0' x 6' - 0' will be $81.00. <span class='line-break'> </span>On the line of steps where you propose to place the monument, the lot falls from rear to front to and one half inches to one foot.</p>
<p>Regarding the Welles lots #789 and #790, the iron fence can be removed and all the posts but those at the corners, which will be rehammered and the number of the lot cut for the old mat-erial. As I understand your have decided on this work being done I enclose order card.</p>

<p>Dear Madam:-</p>
<p>The monument covers which we have heretofore put on<span class='line-break'> </span>and taken off without charge have increased in number to such<span class='line-break'> </span>an extent and the labor is so large that we will hereafter<span class='line-break'> </span>have to make a charge when this is done.</p>
<p>The cover of your monument will be taken off this<span class='line-break'> </span>Spring but in the future a charge of $3.00 will be made each<span class='line-break'> </span>year and if you wish the work done please sign and return the<span class='line-break'> </span>enclosed card to me.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1064143">CB10_0259</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when=''>1889-03-12</date></p>
<p>259</p>
<p>S</p>
<p>March 12, 1889.</p>
<p>B.F. Smith, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>We were unable to understand your message by telephone<span class='line-break'> </span>this forenoon.</p>
<p>Since the electric cars began running the interference<span class='line-break'> </span>has been so great that we have been unable to use the telephone<span class='line-break'> </span>with any degree of accuracy, and until the telephone company, to<span class='line-break'> </span>whom we have already made complaint remedy the matter it is absolu<span class='line-break'></span>tely unsafe to attempt to send any message by telephone in regard<span class='line-break'> </span>to anything which is of importance.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>Dear Madam:-</p>
<p>In regard to the bill for repairs on myrtle in your<span class='line-break'> </span>lot I find that the material had to be carried up a flight of<span class='line-break'> </span>steps, which made the labor a much larger item than it otherwise<span class='line-break'> </span>would have been.</p>
<p>Myrtle is very uncertain, and when we set it out we<span class='line-break'> </span>are expected to renew it without further charge if it dies within<span class='line-break'> </span>the year. I desire to have these charges satisfactory to our<span class='line-break'> </span>proprietors, and if you are willing to relieve the Corporation<span class='line-break'> </span>of any further responsibility for the myrtle set out, I will<span class='line-break'> </span>divide the charge and make it $3.75. <p>Respectfully yours,</p>

<h3><a name="page-1064181">CB10_0278</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>278<span class='line-break'> </span>S<span class='line-break'> </span>March 23, 1889.<span class='line-break'> </span>Mr. P. fay,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.<span class='line-break'> </span>Dear Sir:-<span class='line-break'> </span>Your note is received. We work ten hours a day (Satur<span class='line-break'></span>days excepted, when we work nine) from March 1st, to Oct.1st.<span class='line-break'> </span>One half of Oct. nine and one half hours (Saturdays nine), The<span class='line-break'> </span>second half of Oct, the months of Nov. ,Dec. and Jan. nine hours.<span class='line-break'> </span>Feb. nine and one half hours (Saturdays nine).<span class='line-break'> </span>I am willing to pay you thirty cents an hour from April<span class='line-break'> </span>1st, to Dec. 1st; and twenty nine cents an hour from Dec 1st to <span class='line-break'> </span>April 1st.<span class='line-break'> </span>We work every day except Sundays and legal holidays.<span class='line-break'> </span>If you wish to accept these terms I am willing to take<span class='line-break'> </span>you on trial, and you can report here as soon as convenient.<span class='line-break'> </span>Respectfully yours,<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
