<h3><a name="page-1064182">CB10_0279</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>279<span class='line-break'> </span>March, 23 1889.<span class='line-break'> </span>Benj. R Tilton Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Cambridge, Mass.<span class='line-break'> </span>Dear Sir:-<span class='line-break'> </span>In regard to the graves of Caroline L Thwing and Sarah<span class='line-break'> </span>Huckins about which you called, I find the graves were at one time<span class='line-break'> </span>planted with myrtle but as the lot has been without care for some<span class='line-break'> </span>time the myrtle has died out.<span class='line-break'> </span>To properly raise them level with the rest of the lot<span class='line-break'> </span>and resod them will cost eight dollars<span class='line-break'> </span>To raise the grave level and replant the myrtle would<span class='line-break'> </span>cost sixteen dollars.<span class='line-break'> </span>There is a bill of six dollars for care of the lot in<span class='line-break'> </span>1883 now due and as the trustees do not permit me to do work on<span class='line-break'> </span>lots where there are back bills this would have to be paid before<span class='line-break'> </span>any work is done.<span class='line-break'> </span>The fence is in a poor condition and the lot would be<span class='line-break'> </span>improved by removing it leaving only the four posts at the cor<span class='line-break'></span>ners, recutting these, cutting the number of the lot on one of<span class='line-break'> </span>them, filling up and sodding over the post holes. <p>S<span class='line-break'> </span>March 23,1189.<span class='line-break'> </span>Messrs Mosley, [Boyran?] &amp; Co.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.<span class='line-break'> </span>Dear Sirs:-<span class='line-break'> </span>I understand that the Wisconsin Construction Co., now<span class='line-break'> </span>as #3 [Tremont?] St. (rooms 37-8) which rooms have been rented by this<span class='line-break'> </span>corporator, have a proposal from you to remove their safe, and as<span class='line-break'> </span>one is to be moved is to the room from here, I write to ask for<span class='line-break'> </span>what price you will move in from here and deliver a safe, said by<span class='line-break'> </span>the makers to weigh 4 to 5 tons, measuring outside 6'-10' x 4'-7"<span class='line-break'> </span>x 3'-0", you to be responsible for all damage to the safe or buil<span class='line-break'></span>dings. Its [safe here have is or the ground?] floor, and a team can be [the?]<span class='line-break'> </span>[backers?] within 15 feet. The safe is ready to go in at the time that<span class='line-break'> </span>you take out the other safe, and is to be placed where that now stands.<span class='line-break'> </span>Respectfully yours,<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>

<div id="page-1064200">
<h3><a name="page-1064200">CB10_0297</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p> ( 297 )<span class='line-break'> </span># 597-S.<span class='line-break'> </span><date when=''>1889-3-30-</date><span class='line-break'> </span>March, 30  1889 <span class='line-break'> </span>Miss. J. L. Oliver.<span class='line-break'> </span>New York City.</p>
<p>Dear Madam: -</p>
<p>Your note is received.  Unless I am mistaken the lot to<span class='line-break'> </span>which you refer is # 597 Aster Path, overlooking Consecration dell<span class='line-break'> </span>pond .  From the situation of the lot, the sodding and granite are<span class='line-break'> </span>and very hard to keep in order;  the sodding on the banks cannot<span class='line-break'> </span>from the nature of the case be guaranteed as other soddin, and<span class='line-break'> </span>the earths pressure is so great that only constant repairs will<span class='line-break'> </span>keep the granite in order.</p>
<p>To regrade and sod the lot in a proper manner, reset the<span class='line-break'> </span>curbing, secure the joints with proper clamps and run them with <span class='line-break'> </span>molten lead, will cost $ 180.00 ( one hundred and eighty dollars )<span class='line-break'> </span>There are two slate headstones in the lot the base of <span class='line-break'> </span>which has been split with the frost, and that of Mrs. Oliver is<span class='line-break'> </span>Lying on the bank.  In having your stonecutter provide a new base<span class='line-break'> </span>I would suggest that it be made of granite the stones set in a deep <span class='line-break'> </span>socket and secured with molten lead.<span class='line-break'> </span>Respectfully yours,<span class='line-break'> </span>Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<p># 100-S.<span class='line-break'> </span>March, 30 1889<span class='line-break'> </span>Mrs. Ellen R. Barnard<span class='line-break'> </span>#253 Marlborough St. Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Madam : -<span class='line-break'> </span>Your note is received.  The tomb in your lot is not one<span class='line-break'> </span>of the character to which objections and raise in our annual<span class='line-break'> </span>report .  It is an underground tomb with the entrance covered with<span class='line-break'> </span>the soil, and the door can be sealed up at a small expense any<span class='line-break'> </span>time it is desired to discontinue making intements in the tomb.</p>
<p>There appears to be room for about five common graves<span class='line-break'> </span>in the earth outside the tomb.<span class='line-break'> </span>Respectfully yours,<span class='line-break'> </span>Sup't.<span class='line-break'> </span>April 1<span class='line-break'> </span>Henry Murry &amp; Co.<span class='line-break'> </span>2071 Perham</p>

<p>Your note is received, the sodding on all the graves<span class='line-break'> </span>made during the past winter will be put in proper condition as<span class='line-break'> </span>soon as the season is advanced far enough to permit of that being<span class='line-break'> </span>done.</p>
<p>The grave recently made in your lot will be mounded <span class='line-break'> </span>similar to the other graves there, and if you wish anything differ<span class='line-break'></span>ent from that please advise me soon.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>

<div id="page-1064211">
<h3><a name="page-1064211">CB10_0308</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when=''>1889-04-08</date></p>
<p>Walter W. Pike Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>City Clerk, Cambridge, Mass.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>Your note is[sic] regard to the sum needed for the perpetual<span class='line-break'> </span>care of a lot in this cemetery is received. Our Trustees have not<span class='line-break'> </span>established any rate per foot in such cases as the cost of main<span class='line-break'></span>taining the sodding etc. is modified by the location and other<span class='line-break'> </span>conditions.</p>
<p>The average annual expense of such care as is desired,<span class='line-break'> </span>is estimated, according to the blank memorandum enclosed, and va<span class='line-break'></span>ried according to the size, situation of the lot, etc. and a sum is<span class='line-break'> </span>asked which at four per cent will yeild[sic] the amount necessary to<span class='line-break'> </span>meet this. If the monuments or headstones when out of repair are<span class='line-break'> </span>to be renewed, an additional sum is charged depending on the ma<span class='line-break'></span>terial, the amount if delecate[sic] carving, and the present condition<span class='line-break'> </span>of the strucure.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>#2339-S</p>
<p>April 11, 1889.</p>
<p>Mrs. Elisha Atkins,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Madam:-</p>
<p>I am requested by Mr. Wm. Howell Reed to send you the<span class='line-break'> </span>grade of your lot above the avenue. The lot itself  is substant<span class='line-break'></span>ially level across the front line. At the South front corner the<span class='line-break'> </span>avenue is four feet lower than the lot, and it <sup>falls</sup> to four feet ten<span class='line-break'> </span>inches at the North front corner. The distance from the inside<span class='line-break'> </span>line of the present posts to the avenue will be seven feet.</p>
<p>Granite edgestones on the avenue are not permitted, and<span class='line-break'> </span>to prevent any mistake or misunderstanding it is desirable that a<span class='line-break'> </span>drawing of the proposed stone work should be submitted before the<span class='line-break'> </span>stonecutters begin cutting.</p>

<p>April. 17th. 1889.<span class='line-break'> </span>Phillip Hichborn Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span># 3 Mon't. St.  Charlestown, Mass.</p>
<p>Sir: -</p>
<p>In regard to your application for an addition to your lot<span class='line-break'> </span>There does not appear to be any land which can be sold as an addi<span class='line-break'></span>tion to it.<span class='line-break'> </span>Respectfully yours,<span class='line-break'> </span>Sup't.</p>

<div id="page-1064282">
<h3><a name="page-1064282">CB10_0379</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when=''>1889-05-01</date></p>
<p>379</p>
<p>May 1st. 1889.</p>
<p>[#407-408?]-L.</p>
<p>J.W. [B..?] Esq.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>Lot #407 and #408 are enclosed as one lot of triangular<span class='line-break'> </span>shape, by an iron fence.</p>
<p>On account of the peculiar shape of the enclosure, the<span class='line-break'> </span>fence should be removed from both lots at the same time, whenever<span class='line-break'> </span>it is done at all. In each lot there is a large spruce tree the<span class='line-break'> </span>shade from which is so dense that I do not believe it is possible <span class='line-break'> </span>[indecipherable] sod alive immediately under it.</p>
<p>If the fence remains the cost of perpetual care of the <span class='line-break'> </span>sod, the cleaning [of and?] the renewal of one monument, and the<span class='line-break'> </span>painting of the fence while it remains, would be $525.00 (five hun<span class='line-break'></span>dred and twenty five dollars), and if the fence is removed $450.00<span class='line-break'> </span>(four hundred and fifty dollars).</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1064283">
<h3><a name="page-1064283">CB10_0380</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when=''>1889-05-01</date></p>
<p>380</p>
<p>May 1st, 1889.</p>
<p>L.G. Farmer Sec'y.<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston, Mass.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>I notice a permit has been issued to Mr. R.L. Sands to<span class='line-break'> </span>set a stone in Vesper lot #5000 As these graves are under perpet<span class='line-break'></span>ual care permits should be to deliver only.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering Sup't.</p>
<p><date when=''>1889-05-01</date></p>
<p>#1532-S</p>
<p>May 1, 1889.</p>
<p>Dwight Braman, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>To resod your lot at the present grade will cost $60.00.<span class='line-break'> </span>The trees have been regarded as permanent trees and cannot I think<span class='line-break'> </span>well be spared, and for this reason it is not feasible to sell an<span class='line-break'> </span>addition to the lot.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1064284">
<h3><a name="page-1064284">CB10_0381</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><date when=''>1889-05-02</date></p>
<p>381</p>
<p>S</p>
<p>May 2, 1889.</p>
<p>Messrs R. Ross &amp; Son,<span class='line-break'> </span>Cambridge.</p>
<p>Dear Sirs:-</p>
<p>Please deliver at the top of Palm ave near the Cushing<span class='line-break'> </span>monument 750 sq. ft. of sods and at the end of Marigold path on<span class='line-break'> </span>Lime ave 450 ft. On Monday morning we will need 1500 ft at lot<span class='line-break'> </span>#3498 Laurel avenue.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
<p><date when=''>1889-05-02</date></p>
<p>#3314-S</p>
<p>May 2, 1889.</p>
<p>E.M. Warland, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Cambridge.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:-</p>
<p>Your note is received, the foundation for the stone just<span class='line-break'> </span>set could not be made in line with the other two except by build<span class='line-break'></span>ing over the box, which of course could not be done. It is built<span class='line-break'> </span>at the end of the grave as ordered. The others are without found<span class='line-break'></span>ations, and it is a simple matter to move them up in line with the<span class='line-break'> </span>one just set. If you desire this done please let me know.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>0673</p>
<p>#2265-S.</p>
<p><date when='July 18th. 1889.'>1889-07-18</date></p>
<p>Geo. Ticknor Curtis, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Richfield Springs, N. Y.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>I have examined the record and find that an error has <span class='line-break'> </span>been made by which the interment was entered as having been made <span class='line-break'> </span>in lot #2266 instead of your lot #2265.  I have had the record<span class='line-break'> </span>corrected.</p>
<p>I find that the interment is made in tahe right hand rear <span class='line-break'> </span>corner of your lot.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1064577">
<h3><a name="page-1064577">CB10_0674</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>0674</p>
<p>#1792-S.</p>
<p><date when='July 18th. 1889.'>1889-07-18</date></p>
<p>Mrs. S. M. Delano,<span class='line-break'> </span>Bryn Mawr, Pa.</p>
<p>Dear Madam: -</p>
<p>All the work ordered on your lot except the cleaning has <span class='line-break'> </span>been finished and that is under way.  The annual charge for the <span class='line-break'> </span>care of the lot is $8.00 (eight dollars).</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>

<div id="page-1064578">
<h3><a name="page-1064578">CB10_0675</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>0675</p>
<p>#2365-S.</p>
<p><date when='July 18th. 1889.'>1889-07-18</date></p>
<p>Messrs. A. McDonald &amp; Son,<span class='line-break'> </span>Cambridge, Mass.</p>
<p>Dear Sirs: -</p>
<p>A granite curbing can be placed on lot #2365, but the <span class='line-break'> </span>grade will have to remain as now.  A drawing of the proposed curb<span class='line-break'></span>ing should be submitted for approval before the work is begun on it.</p>
<p>I would call your attention to the limit as to width of <span class='line-break'> </span>steps and that border stones are not permitted.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1064579">
<h3><a name="page-1064579">CB10_0676</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>0676</p>
<p>#3258-S.</p>
<p><date when='July 18th. 1889.'>1889-07-18</date></p>
<p>Samuel E. Somerby, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>So. Framingham, Mass.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>I am sorry that the bill for sodding is not satisfactory.<span class='line-break'> </span>Six feet of sod were laid but as newly laid sod will not live <span class='line-break'> </span>unless frequently watered, a charge large enough to cover that has <span class='line-break'> </span>to be made.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't. </p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1064580">
<h3><a name="page-1064580">CB10_0677</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>0677</p>
<p>#3999-S.</p>
<p><date when='July 19th. 1889.'>1889-07-19</date></p>
<p>H. R. Dalton, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>After a careful examination of your lot I find that the <span class='line-break'> </span>short side cannot be changed enough to make an improvement so that <span class='line-break'> </span>I do not think it worth while to disturb the present arrangement.</p>
<p>The foundation will be built centering on the present <span class='line-break'> </span>front line.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>

After you have seen them will you <span class='line-break'> </span>kindly write me whether they are satisfactory, that I may report <span class='line-break'> </span>to the Trustees.</p>

<p>0679</p>
<p>#2216-L.</p>
<p><date when='July 19th. 1889'>1889-07-19</date></p>
<p>Jos. F. Soshier, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>#15 Charles St., Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>If the deed of the 315 square feet of ornamental land <span class='line-break'> </span>sold on the south side of lot #2216 is surrendered to the Corpo<span class='line-break'></span>ration I will sell as an addition to that lot for your burial purposes,<span class='line-break'> </span>provided no fence or enclosure except the corner posts set by the <span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation be placed to mark it, a strip of land five feet wide<span class='line-break'> </span>making an area of 150 square feet at two dollars per square foot<span class='line-break'> </span>and two dollars for deed, and allow you for the ornamental land <span class='line-break'> </span>reconveyed, the price paid for it, fifty cents per foot.<span class='line-break'> </span>This sale to be subject to the approval of the committee on lots.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>J. W. Lovering  Sup't.</p>
</div>

<p>#4934-S.</p>
<p>Aug. 1st. 1899.</p>
<p>Frank Foxcroft, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Cambridge, Mass.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>I have seen the headstone on your lot marked with the <span class='line-break'> </span>name [?Ruth].  A very slight washing would make it clean, except two <span class='line-break'> </span>small red stains that have probably come from cut flowers which <span class='line-break'> </span>were wired.  Our experience is that such stains cannot be removed<span class='line-break'> </span>except by recutting deep enough and as the Corporation would not <span class='line-break'> </span>undertake work of this character, I herewith enclose you a blank <span class='line-break'> </span>application for permit which if you will please fill out with the <span class='line-break'> </span>name of the firm to be employed, sign and areturn to me, a permit will <span class='line-break'> </span>be sent you.</p>

<p>Dear Sir; -</p>
<p>I have seen the headstone on your lot marked with the <span class='line-break'> </span>name Beth. Our experience is that such stains cannot be removed<span class='line-break'> </span>except by recutting deep enough, and as the Corporation would not <span class='line-break'> </span>undertake work of this character, I herewith enclose you a blank <span class='line-break'> </span>application foar permit which if you will please fill out with the <span class='line-break'> </span>name of the firm to be employed, sign and return to me, a permit <span class='line-break'> </span>will be sent you.</p>

Am I <span class='line-break'> </span>to understand from the drawing now sent that you wish it taken down<span class='line-break'> </span>and turned?</p>
<p>I would suggest that detailed instructions be sent for <span class='line-break'> </span>the erection of all work and for the building of foundations even <span class='line-break'> </span>when it seems apparent how the stone should be set, so that delays <span class='line-break'> </span>and mistakes may be avoided.</p>

<p>Dear Sir: -In the matter of the Hutchings headstone I have had an ex<span class='line-break'></span>amination made and find that there is a foundation under the stone <span class='line-break'> </span>intact and level in every respect and with the top coating of ce<span class='line-break'></span>ment broken.</p>
<p>The setter of the stone, probably not having enough of <span class='line-break'> </span>[?illegible] to bring it high enough covered the foundation with a lay<span class='line-break'></span>er of earth and set the stones on that with the present result.</p>

<p>Dear Sirs:-</p>
<p>Five hundred and twenty five dollars the amount original<span class='line-break'></span>ly named to you for the perpetual care of the Cushing lot #3740,<span class='line-break'> </span>included six dollars worth of plants annually, which would supply <span class='line-break'> </span>usually aboaut four dozen of the varieties generally used.</p>
<p>You can judge how many you want better than I can, but <span class='line-break'> </span>I should think that an increase of from seventy five to one hun<span class='line-break'></span>dred and twenty five dollars would provide a sufficiently large<span class='line-break'> </span>number of mixed plants.</p>
<p>This would make the amount to be paid either six or sev<span class='line-break'></span>ven hundred dollars as you prefer, and the agreement would be for <span class='line-break'> </span>nine or thirteen dollars worth of mixed plants, according to the <span class='line-break'> </span>amount paid, without any agreement to ribbon the beds.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>

<p>The perpetual care of lot #4229 including the care of the <span class='line-break'> </span>sod, the two myrtle graves now on the lot, the cleaning and leading <span class='line-break'> </span>of the granite curbing and the cleaning but not the renewal of the <span class='line-break'> </span>marble sarcophagus will cost $750.00 (seven hundred and fifty dol<span class='line-break'></span>lars), with plants; for plants in the borders $100.00 (  one hun<span class='line-break'></span>dred dollars) additional; for filling and watering vase $100.00 (one hun<span class='line-break'></span>dred dollars) additional, if the two myrtle graves are removed $50.[sic]<span class='line-break'> </span>(fifty dollars) less. <p>In regard to the monumenat the trimming or entire removal <span class='line-break'> </span>of one tree will improve matters but little as a monument elaborate<span class='line-break'> </span>ly carved, collects the dirt and dust very fast even when not ex<span class='line-break'></span>posed to the dripping from the trees.  The trees have grown together<span class='line-break'> </span>so long, that the removal of one would leave the other unshapely<span class='line-break'> </span>[illegible]  monument can be cleaned for twenty dollars, but the <span class='line-break'> </span>marble has suffered considerably from exposure to the weather, and <span class='line-break'> </span>cannot be made to look like a new one, though it can be considera<span class='line-break'></span>bly improved.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>J. W. Lovering, Sup't.</p>

<div id="page-1064635">
<h3><a name="page-1064635">CB10_0731</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>731</p>
<p><date when=''>1889-08-10</date></p>
<p>#2365-L.</p>
<p>Aug. 10th. 1889.</p>
<p>Wm. C. Newell. Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>#149 Broad St., Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>In reply to your favor of Aug. 8th. I would say that at <span class='line-break'> </span>each corner of the curbing either a sufficient foundation should be <span class='line-break'> </span>built, or else the stringers should rest on a post with flat top <span class='line-break'> </span>and base, extending down six feet below the surface, to avoid as far <span class='line-break'> </span>as possible any danger from undermining when any excavation is made<span class='line-break'> </span>in the lot.</p>
<p>If each side is in one piece as it should be, no support<span class='line-break'> </span>between the corners is generally needed.  If, as I understand your<span class='line-break'> </span>plan, it is proposed to show seven or eight inches of curbing above<span class='line-break'> </span>the present sod line, and to raise the sod inside of the curbing <span class='line-break'> </span>three or four inches to the level of the step, there is no objec<span class='line-break'></span>tion to the plan, if you prefer to have an enclosure about the lot,<span class='line-break'> </span>but I cannot forbear calling your attention to the fact that more <span class='line-break'> </span>curbings are being removed, then put around the lots, and that the <span class='line-break'> </span>indications are very strong that within a short time, the stone<span class='line-break'> </span>enclosures will be removed as rapidly as the iron fences have been.</p>
<p>The cost of setting the curbing including the loam need<span class='line-break'></span>ed to raise the sod would be $50.00 (fifty dollars) and the resodd<span class='line-break'></span>fng as already written you $48.00 more, or $30.00 (thirty dollars)<span class='line-break'> </span>for seeding; as the lot is sunken, the sod at the back is of no use.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1064636">
<h3><a name="page-1064636">CB10_0732</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>732</p>
<p>If the lot is seeded and the seed does not come up it <span class='line-break'> </span>would be resown any time needed within a year.</p>
<p>If you decidd to seed the lot, it will be taken under<span class='line-break'> </span>perpetual care at the same rate provided  you are willing to wait <span class='line-break'> </span>for the seed to grow into a good sod, which may take some time.</p>
<p>The cost of perpetual care of the lot, in its present<span class='line-break'> </span>condition, including the raising of that portion of the lot now <span class='line-break'> </span>sunken as well as the entire care of the sod, and including also <span class='line-break'> </span>the cleaning but not the renewal of the monument and marker now on <span class='line-break'> </span>lot, will be $325.00 (three hundred and twenty five dollars) with<span class='line-break'></span>out plants; add for each grave covered with myrtle twenty five dol<span class='line-break'></span>lars, and for plants one hundred dollars or more.</p>
<p>If the lot is enclosed with granite according to the <span class='line-break'> </span>plan proposed, it will add to the cost of perpetual care from two <span class='line-break'> </span>to three hundred dollars.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>J. W. Lovering, Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<h3><a name="page-1064656">CB10_0752</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>752</p>
<p><date when=''>1889-08-22</date></p>
<p>#4699-S.</p>
<p>Aug. 22nd. 1889.</p>
<p>Wm. Jewett, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Waverly, Mass.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>Regarding your complaint at the gate office that the <span class='line-break'> </span>myrtle  border on your lot was dead, I find that in 1884 the Corpo<span class='line-break'></span>ration only prepared the ground and did not supply the myrtle in <span class='line-break'> </span>which case no responsibility is assumed.</p>
<p>To keep myrtle in good condition frequent special repairs<span class='line-break'> </span>are needed.</p>
<p>As the border in its present condition is rather unsight<span class='line-break'></span>ly I will have it sodded up.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<div id="page-1064660">
<h3><a name="page-1064660">CB10_0756</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>756</p>
<p><date when=''>1889-08-24</date></p>
<p>Aug. 24th. 1889.</p>
<p>Messrs. O. &amp; G. Norcross, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston, Mass.</p>
<p>Dear Sirs: -</p>
<p>Your note is received and will have attention.</p>
<p>The $75.00 (Seventy five dollars) is for additional <span class='line-break'> </span>plants.</p>
<p>The grass on newly sodded lots is purposely left long un<span class='line-break'></span>til the sod is properly established and this extra length gives <span class='line-break'> </span>the grass a rather coarse appearance.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1064661">
<h3><a name="page-1064661">CB10_0757</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>757</p>
<p><date when=''>1889-08-24</date></p>
<p>-S.</p>
<p>Aug. 24th. 1889.</p>
<p>J. H. Arnold, Esq.,</p>
<p>Librarian, Law School of Harvard University,<span class='line-break'> </span>Cambridge Mass.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>Your note of Aug. 22nd, is received.  According to our <span class='line-break'> </span>records Frank S. Gerard died at Cambridge Dec. 20th. 1876 and was <span class='line-break'> </span>buried in the receiving tomb of this Cemetery Dec. 22nd.  The re<span class='line-break'></span>mains were afterwards removed to lot #4445, owned by Mrs. Wm. Bates <span class='line-break'> </span>of Cambridge.</p>
<p>Wm. Cowan died June 11th, 1840 and on July 14th, was <span class='line-break'> </span>buried in Harvard College lot (330).  this I have no doubt is <span class='line-break'> </span>the Wm. H. Cowan to whom you refer.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1064669">CB10_0765</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>765</p>
<p><date when=''>1889-08-28</date></p>
<p>#4158-S</p>
<p>Aug. 28th. 1889.</p>
<p>Miss. P. B. Dickinson,<span class='line-break'> </span>Romeo, Mich.</p>
<p>Dear Madam: -</p>
<p>I think the monument you have in mind is a cross erected <span class='line-break'> </span>by Mrs. Jarvis Williams in memory of her husband, on the arms of <span class='line-break'> </span>the cross is the word "IMPLICITLY" and on the base belowe, between <span class='line-break'> </span>the inscription are the words, and not until death, but forever <span class='line-break'> </span>and ever.</p>
<p>The Dickinson lot on Hibiscus path is in good condition.<span class='line-break'> </span>There are two chairs, two bouquet holders and a large vase now <span class='line-break'> </span>on it.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1064671">
<h3><a name="page-1064671">CB10_0767</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>767</p>
<p><date when=''>1889-09-03</date></p>
<p>Sept. 3rd. [188]9</p>
<p>C. W. Cotting, Esq.,</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>When I went <span class='line-break'> </span>in the Bourne tomb with you,<span class='line-break'> </span>to examine the roof and the <span class='line-break'> </span>tiler, you certainly did<span class='line-break'> </span>request that the coffins be <span class='line-break'> </span>protected from the eyes of the <span class='line-break'> </span>curious while the tomb was <span class='line-break'> </span>open, by a covering of boards.</p>
<p>After that, however, I received <span class='line-break'> </span>a message ([?] W<sup>m</sup> Pope I think)<span class='line-break'> </span>asking tht a rough board veti<span class='line-break'></span>bule be put up, and on men<span class='line-break'></span>tioning what you have said<span class='line-break'> </span>about the coming of the coffins<span class='line-break'> </span>I was told the vestibule was what<span class='line-break'> </span>was wanted &amp; I understood that<span class='line-break'> </span>it was to take the place of the covering.</p>
<p>I regret that there should have <span class='line-break'> </span>been any istake in crrying <span class='line-break'> </span>out your wishes, as special <span class='line-break'> </span>[?] have been taken to have<span class='line-break'> </span>them carried out to the letter.</p>
<p>The tiling has been relaid <span class='line-break'> </span>where thrown, and is now in <span class='line-break'> </span>asgood order I think, as possible <span class='line-break'> </span>with the present tiles, and the <span class='line-break'> </span>leading has been repaired.<span class='line-break'> </span>Do you wish the vestibule to remain longer?</p>
<p>Yrs truly,<span class='line-break'> </span>J. W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<div id="page-1064675">
<h3><a name="page-1064675">CB10_0771</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>771</p>
<p><date when=''>1889-09-04</date></p>
<p>#1158-L.</p>
<p>Sept. 4th. 1889.</p>
<p>Mrs. Mary D. Chapman,<span class='line-break'> </span>#[illegible ] St., Springfield, Mass.</p>
<p>Dear Madam: -</p>
<p>You can pay ato the corporation $800.00 (eight hundred<span class='line-break'> </span>dollars) as a donation in trust and the income <sup>will be</sup>expended in keep<span class='line-break'></span>ing lot #1158 and the tomb thereon in repair as far as it is suf<span class='line-break'></span>ficient, but the perpetual care of the lot with guaranty can not <span class='line-break'> </span>be undertaken unless both parts of the tomb are provided for.</p>
<p>Where tombs do not contain separate compartments for <span class='line-break'> </span>each interment, which can be sealed with brick and cement, the Cor<span class='line-break'></span>poration will not undertake the perpetual care with guaranty, unless<span class='line-break'> </span>under condition  that no more interments be made in the tomb or with <span class='line-break'> </span>provision that the Trustees of the Cemetery may remove said tomb <span class='line-break'> </span>should they consider it unsafe or unhealthy, and order all future <span class='line-break'> </span>interments to be made in the ground.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1064700">CB10_0796</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>796</p>
<p><date when=''>1889-09-13</date></p>
<p>L.</p>
<p>Sept. 13. 1889.</p>
<p>Messrs. Scull &amp; Bradley,<span class='line-break'> </span># [?] Water St., Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sirs: -</p>
<p>It is proposed to construct an additional green-house <span class='line-break'> </span>on the North end of the boiler house now insured through your firm<span class='line-break'> </span>in the Royal Insurance Co.  The new house will about 70by28 feet<span class='line-break'> </span>and built of masonry with iron and glass room and very little <span class='line-break'> </span>wood about it.  It will be heated by hot water.</p>
<p>The green-house will be constructed very slowly and may be <span class='line-break'> </span>some three months in building.  I do not want to insure this house <span class='line-break'> </span>until finished but wish to obtain a permit from the company so that <span class='line-break'> </span>the present insurance may not be affected.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1064701">CB10_0797</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>797</p>
<p><date when=''>1889-09-13</date></p>
<p>#3380 -S.</p>
<p>Sept. 13th. 1889.</p>
<p>Edwin D. Ruggles, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>New York.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>The cost to clean all the marble stones in your lot will <span class='line-break'> </span>be $20.00 (twenty dollars).</p>
<p>The grave not planted with myrtle has been in its present <span class='line-break'> </span>condition for some time and the order did not indicate that new<span class='line-break'> </span>myrtle was to be planted.  As you desire it, myrtle will be planted<span class='line-break'> </span>there.  The other myrtle graves are in vry good condition consid<span class='line-break'></span>ering they were planted this season.  They cannot be raised higher<span class='line-break'> </span>except by mounding the earth, and a myrtle will not grow on a <span class='line-break'> </span>mound  in this part of the counry, raising the graves any higher <span class='line-break'> </span>would result in the myrtle dying very soon.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sp't.</p>
</div>
</div>

<p><date when=''>1889-09-14</date></p>
<p>#3748-S.</p>
<p>Sept. 14th. 1889.</p>
<p>Mrs. H. M. Laughlin,<span class='line-break'> </span>#19[??] Loctust St., Phil., Penn.</p>
<p>Dear Madam: -</p>
<p>The cost of cleaning the granite curbing on the Putman[sic]<span class='line-break'> </span>lot #3748 would be $7.50 (seven dollars and fifty cents).  The <span class='line-break'> </span>curbing is coming out of place and at the circular joints at the <span class='line-break'> </span>corners badly broken.  It would be made more sightly be refilling<span class='line-break'> </span>the joints with molten lead at a cost of $12.00 (twelve dollars),<span class='line-break'> </span>but in a few years the stone will require resetting again.</p>
<p>It would improve the appearance of the lot to remove <span class='line-break'> </span>the curbing around it and the border stones next the avenue, leav<span class='line-break'></span>ing only the entrance posts and the posts that mark the boundaries.</p>
<p>Regarding the size of the lot of which something was said <span class='line-break'> </span>at the office there are only 270 ft. in the whole enclosure.  In <span class='line-break'> </span>the Longfellow lot there are 399 ft.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>J. W. Lovering Sup't.<span class='line-break'> </span>Per J. G. S.</p>

<p><date when=''>1889-09-26</date></p>
<p>Sept. 26th. 1889.</p>
<p>#3740-L</p>
<p>Messrs. C. &amp; G. H. Norcross,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>I regret that the provision about plants in the contract <span class='line-break'> </span>for the perpetal care of lot #3740 does not meet your views, but <span class='line-break'> </span>as the varieties of plants available, and the methods of planting <span class='line-break'> </span>vary so greatly from time to time, it seems necessary to limit <span class='line-break'> </span>the amount for plants and care of them to a definite annual expen<span class='line-break'></span>diture.</p>
<p>All the contracts for perpetual care are subject to the <span class='line-break'> </span>approval of the Trustees of the Cemetery and I doubt whether they <span class='line-break'> </span>will approve of any contract which does not limit the work to be  <span class='line-break'> </span>done, or which requires special treatment.</p>
<p>The changes in regard to the cleaning of the monument <span class='line-break'> </span>and title of the contracting parties can no doubt be arranged <span class='line-break'> </span>satisfactorily,</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>

<div id="page-1064747">
<h3><a name="page-1064747">CB10_0843</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>843</p>
<p>Sept. 27th. 1889.</p>
<p>Miss. Ellen D. Putnam,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Madam: -</p>
<p>From your note it would seem that the monument to Judge <span class='line-break'> </span>Putnam is expected to stand nearly in the centre of the lot, and <span class='line-break'> </span>at the same time be nearly at the head of his grave, which on ac<span class='line-break'></span>count of the position of the grave is impossible.  The grave is <span class='line-break'> </span>opposite the steps but at the extreme rear of the lot, and if the<span class='line-break'> </span>monument is placed at the head of the grave it will be opposite the <span class='line-break'> </span>steps but at the extreme back of the lot;  if placed in the centre<span class='line-break'> </span>of the lot, it will be at the foot of Judge Putnam's grave.  I re<span class='line-break'></span>gret to trouble you in the matter, but as the foundation has been <span class='line-break'> </span>built according to instructions at the head of the grave, and next <span class='line-break'> </span>to Katherine's stone, it is desireable if there is a mistake to <span class='line-break'> </span>correct it now.</p>
<p>The other two stones will be set today and the large on <span class='line-break'> </span>as soon as I hear from you.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<div id="page-1064757">
<h3><a name="page-1064757">CB10_0853</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>853</p>
<p>Oct. 1st. 1889.</p>
<p>[C?] H. Crosby, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>#13 Herald Building, Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>The annual payment of $12.00 (twelve dollars) made by <span class='line-break'> </span>Capt. Allen has been for cutting the grass and plants in vases,<span class='line-break'> </span>but did not include any repairs to sod, myrtle or steps, nor the <span class='line-break'> </span>cleaning of the stonework, for all of which an additional expendi<span class='line-break'></span>ture will be needed from time to time if the lot is to be kept in <span class='line-break'> </span>good order.</p>
<p>Six hundred dollars will be received as a Donation in <span class='line-break'> </span>Trust and the income spent in keeping the lot in order as far as <span class='line-break'> </span>it proves sufficient, but without any agreement on the part of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation the income will be sufficieint.</p>
<p>If a contract with guaranty for the perpetual care of the <span class='line-break'> </span>lot is desired, the sum can only be reduced by dispensing with the <span class='line-break'> </span>flowers or myrtle.</p>
<p>The differencae between the two forms of contract amounts<span class='line-break'> </span>to this, that where the money is paid as a Donation in Trust, the <span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation has no liability beond spending the income faithfully <span class='line-break'> </span>but where it is paid for perpetual care with guaranty, the Corpora<span class='line-break'></span>tion assumes the risk of all changes in the rate of interest, and <span class='line-break'> </span>the price of labor and water also needed to keep the lot in order.</p>
<p>Yours truly, J. W. Lovering, Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1064770">
<h3><a name="page-1064770">CB10_0866</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>866</p>
<p>-L.</p>
<p>Oct. 9 th 1889.</p>
<p>Charles H. Lord, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>P. O. Box #2262, Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>I regret that there has been any delay in answering your <span class='line-break'> </span>inquiry about repairing the monument on the Hayes lot.</p>
<p>A careful examination shows that the repairs would prob<span class='line-break'></span>ably cost nearly one hundred dollars and possibly more, and there <span class='line-break'> </span>is not enough unexpended income to meet so large an expense at <span class='line-break'> </span>this time.</p>
<p>Moreover from the general condition of the monument it <span class='line-break'> </span>is doubtful if it is worth so large an expenditure.</p>
<p>Respectfully ours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<p>#2013 - S.</p>
<p>Oct. 9 th. 1889.</p>
<p>Capt. G. B. Wadleigh,<span class='line-break'> </span>Navy Yard, Charlestown, Mass.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>The cost to properly scrape and paint the fence on lot<span class='line-break'> </span>#2013 will be $8.00 (eight dollars).</p>
<p>The fence is in a very rusty condition and it is going <span class='line-break'> </span>to decay very fast.  It would improve the lot to remove the fence<span class='line-break'> </span>and all the posts except four corner posts, these four rehammered<span class='line-break'> </span>and the number of the lot cut on one of them, which can be done for <span class='line-break'> </span>the old material.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>

<p>-L.</p>
<p>Oct. 10 th. 1889.</p>
<p>Charles F. Dowse, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>#229 Franklin Street,Boston.</p>
<p>Der Sir: -</p>
<p>Enclosed please find map of Cemetery.</p>
<p>A lot of 300 square feet with the perpetual care of the <span class='line-break'> </span>grass costs from $575.00 (five hundred and seventy five dollars) to<span class='line-break'> </span>$810.00 (eight hundred and ten dollars) according to the location <span class='line-break'> </span>and smaller lots can be had at a reduction, say from $300.00 (three<span class='line-break'> </span>hundred dollars) to $500.00 (five hundred dollars).  You will get <span class='line-break'> </span>a more satisfactory idea of the lots on the ground, and some one <span class='line-break'> </span>will be sent with you to point them out on any week day.</p>

<div id="page-1064773">
<h3><a name="page-1064773">CB10_0869</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>869</p>
<p>#1339-L.</p>
<p>Oct. 10th. 1889.</p>
<p>Mrs. Mabel Thayer Jacassy,<span class='line-break'> </span>Care Messrs. W. J. Turner &amp; Co,<span class='line-break'> </span>Bankers,<span class='line-break'> </span>Maples [sic], Italy.</p>
<p>Dear Madam: -</p>
<p>Your letter of Sept. 15th. in regard to the perpetual car<span class='line-break'> </span>care of lot #1339 has been received.  I regret very much that there <span class='line-break'> </span>was any oversight about the myrtle which was planted the day after <span class='line-break'> </span>the ommission was discovered.</p>
<p>In other respects the lot has received frequent and con<span class='line-break'></span>sistant care each season, it having been cut with lawn mover once in <span class='line-break'> </span>ten days, and sometimes oftener; grass seed and fertilizer have<span class='line-break'> </span>been put on several times; the monument has been cleaned for times <span class='line-break'> </span>this year alone.</p>
<p>There are on adjoining lots three oak trees which over<span class='line-break'></span>hang the monument, and the dripping from these trees cause a stain <span class='line-break'> </span>after every shower, during June and July, which is remoevd with <span class='line-break'> </span>as little delay as possible.</p>
<p>Please advice me in detail as to just what you consider <span class='line-break'> </span>unsatisfactory.</p>
<p>Yours truly,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1064775">
<h3><a name="page-1064775">CB10_0871</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>871</p>
<p>#2265-S.</p>
<p>Oct. 10th. 1889.</p>
<p>A. R. Alison, Esq.</p>
<p>Newport, R. I.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>I have examined your lot and it does not appear to me <span class='line-break'> </span>that anything could be accomplished by merely spreading some loam <span class='line-break'> </span>on the present survace.</p>
<p>To get anything of a sod about six loads of loam and one <span class='line-break'> </span>of manure should be added to the present soil, the whole spaded<span class='line-break'> </span>up and sown with grass seed.  The expense of this would be $25.00<span class='line-break'> </span>(twenty five dollars).</p>
<p>To keep  the lot in order and secure any result from this <span class='line-break'> </span>an order for the regular care should be gien.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>

The cost of a foundation in Miss.<span class='line-break'> </span>[illegible] lot [?'] - 8"  by 3' - 8"  will be $48.50 (forty-eight dollars <span class='line-break'> </span>and fifty cents. As all work except such <span class='line-break'> </span>[illegible] ordered by proprietors on their own lot is payable in advance<span class='line-break'> </span>the amount will have to be prepaid.  The exact location in which <span class='line-break'> </span>the monument will stand in the lot should be given, and if there <span class='line-break'> </span>are [illegible] should be stated.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1064820">CB10_0916</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>916</p>
<p>#2404 - L.</p>
<p>Oct. 29th. 1889.</p>
<p>Charles H. Cotting, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>The perpetual care of the Phillip's lot #2404 including <span class='line-break'> </span>the care and renewal of the structures on the lot is worth four <span class='line-break'> </span>thousand dollars.</p>
<p>Several years ago the Trustees voted not to take under <span class='line-break'> </span>perpetual care with guaranty any chamber tomb with entrance opening <span class='line-break'> </span>above ground, except under the condition that no more interments <span class='line-break'> </span>be [?] the tomb, or [?] the provision that the Trustees of <span class='line-break'> </span>the Cemetery may remove the tomb should they consider it unsafe <span class='line-break'> </span>or unhealthy  and order all future interments made in the ground.</p>
<p>As I understand it the coffins are now placed on shelves <span class='line-break'> </span>and can probably be picked up, so as to come within the spirit<span class='line-break'> </span>of the vote.</p>
<p>There are several small breaks on the post and buttresses <span class='line-break'> </span>and in making his estimate the immediate renewal of thes pieces <span class='line-break'> </span>was not contemplated.</p>
<p>Respectfully yoyurs,</p>
<p>Sp't.</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>If the border stone, four buttresses and flat platform <span class='line-break'> </span>were removed, the appearance of the lot would be very much improv<span class='line-break'></span>ed and the continued expense of resetting the stones avoided.</p>
<p>The Corporation will remove the stone and sod over the<span class='line-break'> </span>place for the old material.</p>
<p>To regrade and sod the lot would cost $45.00 (forty five<span class='line-break'> </span>dollars).</p>
<p>To remove the curbing, set four eight inch boundary posts, <span class='line-break'> </span>cut the number of the lot, lower the monument and headstones to new<span class='line-break'> </span>grade ond regrade and sod the whole lot would cost $45.00 (forty<span class='line-break'> </span>five dollars) and the old material.</p>

<p>942</p>
<p>-S.</p>
<p>Nov. 6th. 1889.</p>
<p>Mrs. M. H. Dehom,<span class='line-break'> </span>#273 Fifth Ave., New York.</p>
<p>Dear Madam: -</p>
<p>I enclose you a map with the locations of some of the <span class='line-break'> </span>unsold lots marked.  All these lots are substantially ready for use<span class='line-break'> </span>and a removal could be made 48 hours after the lot is paid for.</p>
<p>A removal could probably be made up to Dec. 1st. and there are usu<span class='line-break'></span>ally days in Dec. when such work can be done.</p>
<p>Before a removal is made, an order signed by a majority <span class='line-break'> </span>of the heirs (if not owned by one person) of the lot from which the <span class='line-break'> </span>remains are to be taken and by theproprietor of the new lot, has <span class='line-break'> </span>to be sent here, and the location of the grave in the new lot should<span class='line-break'> </span>be exactly designated by diagram or otherwise.</p>
<p>The amount needed for the perpetual care of a lot would <span class='line-break'> </span>depend on its situation etc. so that I would need to know the par<span class='line-break'></span>ticular lot before an estimate is made.</p>
<p>Respectfyully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>

<p>948</p>
<p>#1104 - #41-L.</p>
<p>Nov. 8th. 1889.</p>
<p>C. H. Saunders, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span># 50 North Avenue, Cambridge, Mass.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>You can pay over as a donation in trust for the care of <span class='line-break'> </span>lot #1105 such sum of money exceeding one hundred dollars as you <span class='line-break'> </span>wish to appropriate to the purpose, and the income will be spent <span class='line-break'> </span>in keeping the lot in order as far as it proves sufficient.</p>
<p>If, however, you prefer to place the lot under perpetual<span class='line-break'> </span>care with guaranty, the care of the curbing around the whole enclos<span class='line-break'></span>ure must be provided for.</p>
<p>The cost of perpetual care of the whole enclosure (lots<span class='line-break'> </span>1105 and #41), including the care of the sod and myrtle now on the <span class='line-break'> </span>lots, the resetting and leading of the curbing while it lasts and <span class='line-break'> </span>the washing but not the renewal of the headstones, will be $1450.00<span class='line-break'> </span>(fourteen hundred and fifty dollars), a reduction of $150.00 (one<span class='line-break'> </span>hundred and fifty dollars) will be made, if the curbstones on the <span class='line-break'> </span>avenue line on each side of the steps are removed, and a further <span class='line-break'> </span>reduction of $225.00 (two hundred and twenty five dollars) if all <span class='line-break'> </span>the myrtle graves are removed.</p>
<p>The cost of perpetual care of lot #1105 alone including <span class='line-break'> </span>the care of the sod and myrtle, the cleaning but not the renewal of <span class='line-break'> </span>the headstones and the resetting and leading of the entire curbing <span class='line-break'> </span>as long as it lasts, will be $950.00(nine hundred and fifty dollars<span class='line-break'> </span>or if the edgestones on the side of the steps is removed a further <span class='line-break'> </span>reduction of $125.00 (one hundred and twenty five dollars) will <span class='line-break'> </span>be made.</p>

<div id="page-1064870">
<h3><a name="page-1064870">CB10_0966</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>966</p>
<p>Nov. 16th. 1889.</p>
<p>Mrs. H. H. Dehon,<span class='line-break'> </span>#273  Fifth Avenue, New York.</p>
<p>Dear Madam: -</p>
<p>The brown-stone posts under the fence are in very poor condi<span class='line-break'></span>tion, and unless replaced soon, the fence must be removed.  They <span class='line-break'> </span>should be replaced, if at all, with a more durable stone, which <span class='line-break'> </span>would make it necessary to replace all the stonework, the expense of <span class='line-break'> </span>which would be entirely out of proprotion to the results obtained.</p>
<p>Contracts are not made for the perpetual care of less than a <span class='line-break'> </span>whole lot, but after the lot has been arranged as desired you can pro<span class='line-break'></span>bably come to soem understanding with the owner of the other art,<span class='line-break'> </span>so that the perpetual care of teh whole can be provided for.</p>
<p>To regrade and sod the whole enclosure would cost one hundred<span class='line-break'> </span>and forty dollars ($140.00) and to regrade and sod one half of it <span class='line-break'> </span>would cost eighty dollars ($80.00).  If the whole lot were regraded<span class='line-break'> </span>and sown with grass seed the expense would be seventy dollars ($70.00)<span class='line-break'> </span>or forty dollars ($40.00) for half teh lot and although you would <span class='line-break'> </span>have to wait longer, our experience is that the results are fully as <span class='line-break'> </span>good.  The grass will not grow well under the two trees that remain,<span class='line-break'> </span>but until the room is needed for interments, I think it would be a <span class='line-break'> </span>pity to remove them.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours, <span class='line-break'> </span>J. W. Lovering Sup't.<span class='line-break'> </span>per [illegible]<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1064877">CB10_0973</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>973<span class='line-break'> </span>[Note: pg 974 missing.  On pg. 973, written by hand diagonally across the page top and bottom:<span class='line-break'> </span>VOID SEE PAGE 977]</p>
<p>[Text of letter follows:]</p>
<p>#2216-L.</p>
<p>Nov. 19th. 1889.</p>
<p>P.C. Welch, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>#5 Tremont St., Room #51, Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>The estimate of one thousand dollars for the perpetual <span class='line-break'> </span>care of lot #2216 includes the care and repairs of the sodding up<span class='line-break'></span>on all the land inside the fence and upon such pieces outside as<span class='line-break'> </span>are owned by the Sohier family in connection with the lot, the <span class='line-break'> </span>strip on the top of the bank wall being one; also the care of <span class='line-break'> </span>the myrtle and peony, the covering with wooden box of the cross, <span class='line-break'> </span>the washing and pointing, but not the renewal of the monument and <span class='line-break'> </span>headstones, the repairing of the bank wall at rear, and the paint<span class='line-break'></span>ting of the iron fence while it lasts.</p>
<p>The covering of the myrtle is never specified in the acon<span class='line-break'></span>tracts, but it is protected in whatever seems to be a suitable way.</p>
<p>The peony was removed from the lot to greenhouse during <span class='line-break'> </span>certain changes and repairs, and will be set out again, but it is <span class='line-break'> </span>not understood that it requires to be taken up and stored at the <span class='line-break'> </span>greenhouse each Winter and such care is not included.</p>
<p>The bill of thirty six dollars ($36.00) was for the foun<span class='line-break'></span>dation of the monument, and that of four dollars and ninety cents <span class='line-break'> </span>($4.90) for the foundation and setting of a small marker.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1064890">CB10_0986</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>986</p>
<p>#4199-L.</p>
<p>Nov. 23rd. 1889.</p>
<p>Thomas Doliber, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>#41 Central Wharf, Boston.</p>
<p>You can pay the Corporation three hundred dollars ($300.00)<span class='line-break'> </span>in trust and the income will be spent on the care of the lot, as <span class='line-break'> </span>far as it proves efficient, whether it does or not, depending on <span class='line-break'> </span>the rate of interest and the cost of labor.</p>
<p>In making the cost of perpetual care with guaranty four <span class='line-break'> </span>hundred and seventy five dollars ($475.00), the washing of the head<span class='line-break'></span>stones and the repairing of the sod is included for both of which <span class='line-break'> </span>you would pay in addition to the amount now paid annually, and as <span class='line-break'> </span>the Corporation agrees in a contract with guaranty to keep the lot <span class='line-break'> </span>in good order, there must of course be a margin to cover fluctua<span class='line-break'></span>tions in cost of labor, or rate of interest;  in otherwords, in <span class='line-break'> </span>the latter form of contract the Corporation takes the risk of the <span class='line-break'> </span>cost of labor and rate of interest, while in the former the lot<span class='line-break'> </span>owner does, the liability of the Corporation ceasing when the in<span class='line-break'></span>come has been properly expended.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1064907">
<h3><a name="page-1064907">CB10_1003</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>1103</p>
<p>#2603-L.</p>
<p>Dec. 4th. 1889.</p>
<p>[?]W. Holmes, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>Please find enclosed order for the removal of W. H. <span class='line-break'> </span>Manning which sghould be signed by the present owner of the lot of <span class='line-break'> </span>the late Prentiss Robbs.</p>
<p>Do you desire to have the remains on the lot, ready for <span class='line-break'> </span>interment at the hour you name, or do you prefer to send  hearse <span class='line-break'> </span>to take removal from tomb to lot?  If so you should order one of <span class='line-break'> </span>an undertaker as none is furnished at the cemetery.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours.</p>
<p>Dec. 4th [188]9<span class='line-break'> </span>Messrs. Evans &amp; Tombs<span class='line-break'> </span>4412 Foote</p>
<p>Removing stone &amp; resetting one <u>5 00</u></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1064908">
<h3><a name="page-1064908">CB10_1004</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>1004</p>
<p>#1104-S.</p>
<p>Dec. 4th. 1889.</p>
<p>Messrs. Bowker, Torrey &amp; Co.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sirs: -</p>
<p>Enclosed you will find bill for foundation in the Wildes<span class='line-break'> </span>lot.  Will the foundation be built at he end of grave farthest <span class='line-break'> </span>from the path?  I am not sure which way the head is placed.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>J. W. Lovering, Sup't.</p>
<p>Dec. 4th. [188]9</p>
<p>Messrs. Bower, Torrey &amp; Co.<span class='line-break'> </span>1109 Wildes</p>
<p>Building foundation 2'- 4" x1'5"  <u>$40</u></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1064909">
<h3><a name="page-1064909">CB10_1005</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>1005</p>
<p>#2833-S.</p>
<p>Dec. 4th. 1889.</p>
<p>Rufus C. Cushman, Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>#36 Central St., Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir: -</p>
<p>Your message given at the gate office is received.  Will <span class='line-break'> </span>you please tell me on which lot you wished the estimate made, your <span class='line-break'> </span>own lot #2833, or the Mentzer lot #2560, and just what you desire <span class='line-break'> </span>done, as there seems to be some misunderstanding about the matter.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>
<p>#3431-S.</p>
<p>Mrs. M. A. Adams,<span class='line-break'> </span>Melrose Highlands, Mass.</p>
<p>Dear Madam: -</p>
<p>The workmen have gone over the two marble stones again <span class='line-break'> </span>and the green moss has been taken off, but I do not think they can be<span class='line-break'> </span>made to look much better.  The lot has been liberally top-dressed.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1064910">
<h3><a name="page-1064910">CB10_1006</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>1006</p>
<p>#3748-S.</p>
<p>Dec. 6th. 1889.</p>
<p>Mrs. H. H. Laughlin,<span class='line-break'> </span>#1943 Locust St., Phil., Penn.</p>
<p>Dear Madam,</p>
<p>Your note to our Treasurer has been forwarded to me for <span class='line-break'> </span>answer.  The bounds in your lot are irregular in shape, but outside<span class='line-break'> </span>of that the turf is in fair condition.  If the mounds were made<span class='line-break'> </span>flat the turf would be in nearly as good condition as new sod would <span class='line-break'> </span>make it.  The granite curbing is very much out of place, and <span class='line-break'> </span>I would sugfgest that it have attention fiarst.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours,</p>
<p>Sup't.</p>
<p>Dec. 6th [1889]</p>
<p>Messrs. Evans &amp; Tombs<span class='line-break'> </span>1207 Bowditch</p>
<p>Setting monument 1889  <u>15 00</u></p>
</div>
</div>
